<p>The
<a
href="/wiki/Bad_(tour)?qsrc=3044"
title="Bad
(tour)">Bad</a>
world
tour
began
on
September
12
that
year,
finishing
on
January
14,
1989.<sup
id="cite_ref-lewis_95-96_92-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lewis_95-96-92">[93]</a></sup>
In
Japan
alone,
the
tour
had
14
sellouts
and
drew
570,000
people,
nearly
tripling
the
previous
record
of
200,000
in
a
single
tour.<sup
id="cite_ref-WashPost_93-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-WashPost-93">[94]</a></sup>
Jackson
broke
a
<i>Guinness
World
Record</i>
<span
class="Z3988"
title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=&amp;rfr_id=info:sid/en.wikipedia.org:Michael_Jackson"><span
style="display:
none;">&nbsp;</span></span>
when
504,000
people
attended
seven
sold-out
shows
at
<a
href="/wiki/Wembley_Stadium_(1923)?qsrc=3044"
title="Wembley
Stadium
(1923)">Wembley
Stadium</a>.
He
performed
a
total
of
123
concerts
to
an
audience
of
4.4&nbsp;million
people.
The
Bad
Tour
turned
out
to
be
the
last
of
Jackson's
concert
tours
to
include
shows
in
the
continental
United
States,
although
later
tours
did
make
it
to
Hawaii.</p>








<p>In
1988,
Jackson
released
his
only
autobiography,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Moonwalk_(book)?qsrc=3044"
title="Moonwalk
(book)">Moonwalk</a></i>,
which
took
four
years
to
complete
and
sold
200,000
copies.<sup
id="cite_ref-Remembering_Michael_94-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Remembering_Michael-94">[95]</a></sup>
Jackson
wrote
about
his
childhood,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Jackson_5?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Jackson
5">The
Jackson
5</a>,
and
the
abuse
he
had
suffered.<sup
id="cite_ref-jackson10_95-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jackson10-95">[96]</a></sup>
He
also
wrote
about
his
facial
appearance,
saying
he
had
had
two
rhinoplastic
surgeries
and
a
<a
href="/wiki/Cleft_chin?qsrc=3044"
title="Cleft
chin">dimple</a>
created
in
his
chin.<sup
id="cite_ref-jackson_229-230_65-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jackson_229-230-65">[66]</a></sup>
He
attributed
much
of
the
change
in
the
structure
of
his
face
to
<a
href="/wiki/Puberty?qsrc=3044"
title="Puberty">puberty</a>,
weight
loss,
a
strict
vegetarian
diet,
a
change
in
hair
style,
and
stage
lighting.<sup
id="cite_ref-jackson_229-230_65-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jackson_229-230-65">[66]</a></sup>
<i>Moonwalk</i>
reached
the
top
position
on
<i>The
New
York
Times</i>
best
sellers'
list.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_42_96-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_42-96">[97]</a></sup>
The
musician
then
released
a
film
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Moonwalker?qsrc=3044"
title="Moonwalker">Moonwalker</a></i>,
which
featured
live
footage
and
short
films
that
starred
Jackson
and
<a
href="/wiki/Joe_Pesci?qsrc=3044"
title="Joe
Pesci">Joe
Pesci</a>.
The
film
was
originally
intended
to
be
released
to
theaters,
but
due
to
financial
issues,
the
film
was
released
<a
href="/wiki/Direct-to-video?qsrc=3044"
title="Direct-to-video">direct-to-video</a>.
It
saw
a
theatrical
release
in
Germany,
though.
It
debuted
atop
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Top
Music
Video
Cassette
chart,
staying
there
for
22
weeks.
It
was
eventually
knocked
off
the
top
spot
by
<i>Michael
Jackson:
The
Legend
Continues</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_43-44_97-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_43-44-97">[98]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
March
1988,
Jackson
purchased
land
near
<a
href="/wiki/Santa_Ynez,_California?qsrc=3044"
title="Santa
Ynez,
California">Santa
Ynez</a>,
California,
to
build
<a
href="/wiki/Neverland_Ranch?qsrc=3044"
title="Neverland
Ranch">Neverland
Ranch</a>
at
a
cost
of
$17&nbsp;million.
He
installed
<a
href="/wiki/Ferris_wheel?qsrc=3044"
title="Ferris
wheel">Ferris
wheels</a>,
a
<a
href="/wiki/Menagerie?qsrc=3044"
title="Menagerie">menagerie</a>,
and
a
movie
theater
on
the
2,700-acre
(11&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup>)
property.
A
security
staff
of
40
patrolled
the
grounds.
In
2003,
it
was
valued
at
approximately
$100&nbsp;million.<sup
id="cite_ref-rollingstone_98-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rollingstone-98">[99]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-usatoday_finances_99-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-usatoday_finances-99">[100]</a></sup>
In
1989,
his
annual
earnings
from
album
sales,
endorsements,
and
concerts
was
estimated
at
$125&nbsp;million
for
that
year
alone.<sup
id="cite_ref-World_Records_100-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-World_Records-100">[101]</a></sup>
Shortly
afterwards,
he
became
the
first
Westerner
to
appear
in
a
television
ad
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Soviet_Union?qsrc=3044"
title="Soviet
Union">Soviet
Union</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_43-44_97-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_43-44-97">[98]</a></sup></p>








<p>His
success
resulted
in
his
being
dubbed
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Honorific_nicknames_in_popular_music?qsrc=3044"
title="Honorific
nicknames
in
popular
music">King
of
Pop</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-broadcasting_101-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-broadcasting-101">[102]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_coronated_latest_king_of_rock_.27n.27_roll_102-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_coronated_latest_king_of_rock_.27n.27_roll-102">[103]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Is_the_thrill_gone_for_singer_Michael_Jackson.3F_103-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Is_the_thrill_gone_for_singer_Michael_Jackson.3F-103">[104]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson.27s_Black_or_White_Blues_104-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson.27s_Black_or_White_Blues-104">[105]</a></sup>
The
nickname
was
popularized
by
<a
href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Taylor?qsrc=3044"
title="Elizabeth
Taylor">Elizabeth
Taylor</a>
when
she
presented
him
with
the
Soul
Train
Heritage
Award
in
1989,
proclaiming
him
&quot;the
true
king
of
pop,
rock
and
soul.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-campbell_105-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-campbell-105">[106]</a></sup>
President
<a
href="/wiki/George_H.W._Bush?qsrc=3044"
title="George
H.W.
Bush">George
H.W.
Bush</a>
designated
him
the
White
House's
&quot;Artist
of
the
Decade&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-georgebush_106-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-georgebush-106">[107]</a></sup>
From
1985
to
1990,
he
donated
$500,000
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_Negro_College_Fund?qsrc=3044"
title="United
Negro
College
Fund">United
Negro
College
Fund</a>,
and
all
of
the
profits
from
his
single
&quot;Man
in
the
Mirror&quot;
went
to
charity.<sup
id="cite_ref-Blacks_who_give_back_107-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Blacks_who_give_back-107">[108]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli11_108-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli11-108">[109]</a></sup>
Jackson's
live
rendition
of
&quot;You
Were
There&quot;
at
<a
href="/wiki/Sammy_Davis,_Jr.?qsrc=3044"
title="Sammy
Davis,
Jr.">Sammy
Davis
Jr.'s</a>
60th
birthday
celebration
allowed
Jackson
to
receive
his
second
Emmy
nomination.<sup
id="cite_ref-emmys.tv_45-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-emmys.tv-45">[46]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_43-44_97-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_43-44-97">[98]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Dangerous.2C_Heal_the_World_Foundation_and_Super_Bowl_XXVII_.281991.E2.80.9393.29"><i>Dangerous</i>,
Heal
the
World
Foundation
and
Super
Bowl
XXVII
(1991–93)</span></h3>








<p>In
March
1991,
Jackson
renewed
his
contract
with
Sony
for
$65
million,
a
record-breaking
deal
at
the
time,<sup
id="cite_ref-mtv_109-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mtv-109">[110]</a></sup>
displacing
<a
href="/wiki/Neil_Diamond?qsrc=3044"
title="Neil
Diamond">Neil
Diamond</a>'s
renewal
contract
with
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia_Records?qsrc=3044"
title="Columbia
Records">Columbia
Records</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Deal_record_110-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Deal_record-110">[111]</a></sup>
He
released
his
eighth
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dangerous_(Michael_Jackson_album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Dangerous
(Michael
Jackson
album)">Dangerous</a></i>
in
1991.
As
of
2008,
<i>Dangerous</i>
had
shipped
seven
million
copies
in
the
U.S.
and
had
sold
32&nbsp;million
copies
worldwide.
The
<i>Dangerous</i>
album
was
co-produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Teddy_Riley_(producer)?qsrc=3044"
title="Teddy
Riley
(producer)">Teddy
Riley</a>,
one
of
the
pioneers
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/New_jack_swing?qsrc=3044"
title="New
jack
swing">new
jack
swing</a>&quot;
which
convinced
Michael
to
feature
a
<a
href="/wiki/Rapping?qsrc=3044"
title="Rapping">rapper</a>
on
his
album
for
the
first
time,
the
act
worked
and
it
turned
out
to
be
the
best-selling
album
associated
with
that
movement.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_certifications_111-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA_certifications-111">[112]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Dangerous_32_million_copies_worldwide_112-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Dangerous_32_million_copies_worldwide-112">[113]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-New_jack_swing_113-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-New_jack_swing-113">[114]</a></sup>
In
the
United
States,
the
album's
first
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Black_or_White?qsrc=3044"
title="Black
or
White">Black
or
White</a>&quot;
was
its
biggest
hit,
reaching
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot&nbsp;100
and
remaining
there
for
seven
weeks,
with
similar
chart
performances
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_achievements_114-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_achievements-114">[115]</a></sup>
The
album's
second
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Remember_the_Time?qsrc=3044"
title="Remember
the
Time">Remember
the
Time</a>&quot;
spent
eight
weeks
in
the
top
five
in
the
United
States,
peaking
at
number
three
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
Hot&nbsp;100
singles
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_45-46_115-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_45-46-115">[116]</a></sup>
At
the
end
of
1992,
<i>Dangerous</i>
was
awarded
1992's
best-selling
album
worldwide
and
&quot;Black
or
White&quot;
was
awarded
1992's
best-selling
single
worldwide
at
the
Billboard
Music
Awards.
Additionally,
he
won
an
award
as
best-selling
artist
of
the
1980s.<sup
id="cite_ref-Best_1992_116-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Best_1992-116">[117]</a></sup>
In
1993,
Jackson
performed
the
song
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Soul_Train_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
title="Soul
Train
Music
Awards">Soul
Train
Music
Awards</a>
in
a
chair,
saying
he
had
suffered
an
injury
in
rehearsals.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli12_117-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli12-117">[118]</a></sup>
In
the
UK
and
other
parts
of
Europe,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Heal_the_World?qsrc=3044"
title="Heal
the
World">Heal
the
World</a>&quot;
was
the
biggest
hit
from
the
album;
it
sold
450,000
copies
in
the
UK
and
spent
five
weeks
at
number
two
in
1992.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_45-46_115-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_45-46-115">[116]</a></sup></p>








<p>Jackson
founded
the
<a
href="/wiki/Heal_the_World_Foundation?qsrc=3044"
title="Heal
the
World
Foundation">Heal
the
World
Foundation</a>
in
1992.
The
charity
organization
brought
underprivileged
children
to
Jackson's
ranch
to
enjoy
theme
park
rides
that
Jackson
had
built
on
the
property.
The
foundation
also
sent
millions
of
dollars
around
the
globe
to
help
children
threatened
by
war,
poverty,
and
disease.
In
the
same
year
Jackson
published
his
second
book,
the
bestselling
collection
of
poetry,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dancing_the_Dream?qsrc=3044"
title="Dancing
the
Dream">Dancing
the
Dream</a></i>.
While
it
was
a
commercial
success
and
revealed
a
more
intimate
side
to
Jackson's
nature,
the
collection
was
mostly
critically
unacclaimed
at
the
time
of
release.
In
2009,
the
book
was
republished
by
<a
href="/wiki/Doubleday_(publisher)?qsrc=3044"
title="Doubleday
(publisher)">Doubleday</a>
and
was
more
positively
received
by
some
critics
in
the
wake
of
Jackson's
untimely
death.
The
<a
href="/wiki/Dangerous_World_Tour?qsrc=3044"
title="Dangerous
World
Tour">Dangerous
World
Tour</a>
grossed
<span
class="nowrap">$100
million</span>.
The
tour
began
on
June
27,
1992,
and
finished
on
November
11,
1993.
Jackson
performed
to
3.5&nbsp;million
people
in
70
concerts.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_45-46_115-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_45-46-115">[116]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_to_Tour_Overseas_118-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_to_Tour_Overseas-118">[119]</a></sup>
He
sold
the
broadcast
rights
to
his
<i>Dangerous</i>
world
tour
to
<a
href="/wiki/HBO?qsrc=3044"
title="HBO">HBO</a>
for
$20&nbsp;million,
a
record-breaking
deal
that
still
stands.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli13_119-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli13-119">[120]</a></sup></p>








<p>Following
the
illness
and
death
of
<a
href="/wiki/Ryan_White?qsrc=3044"
title="Ryan
White">Ryan
White</a>,
Jackson
helped
draw
public
attention
to
HIV/AIDS,
something
that
was
still
controversial
at
the
time.
He
publicly
pleaded
with
the
<a
href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Bill_Clinton?qsrc=3044"
title="Presidency
of
Bill
Clinton">Clinton
Administration</a>
at
Bill
Clinton's
Inaugural
Gala
to
give
more
money
to
HIV/AIDS
charities
and
research.<sup
id="cite_ref-Stars_line_up_for_Clinton_celebration_120-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Stars_line_up_for_Clinton_celebration-120">[121]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Facing_the_music_and_the_masses_at_the_presidential_gala_121-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Facing_the_music_and_the_masses_at_the_presidential_gala-121">[122]</a></sup>
In
a
high-profile
visit
to
Africa,
Jackson
visited
several
countries,
among
them
<a
href="/wiki/Gabon?qsrc=3044"
title="Gabon">Gabon</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Egypt?qsrc=3044"
title="Egypt">Egypt</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ebony_122-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ebony-122">[123]</a></sup>
His
first
stop
to
Gabon
was
greeted
with
a
sizable
and
enthusiastic
reception
of
more
than
100,000
people,
some
of
them
carrying
signs
that
read,
&quot;Welcome
Home
Michael.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Ebony_122-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ebony-122">[123]</a></sup>
In
his
trip
to
<a
href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire?qsrc=3044"
title="C&ocirc;te
d'Ivoire">C&ocirc;te
d'Ivoire</a>,
Jackson
was
crowned
&quot;King
Sani&quot;
by
a
tribal
chief.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ebony_122-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ebony-122">[123]</a></sup>
He
then
thanked
the
dignitaries
in
French
and
English,
signed
official
documents
formalizing
his
kingship
and
sat
on
a
golden
throne
while
presiding
over
ceremonial
dances.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ebony_122-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ebony-122">[123]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
January
1993,
Jackson
made
a
memorable
appearance
at
the
halftime
show
at
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXVII?qsrc=3044"
title="Super
Bowl
XXVII">Super
Bowl&nbsp;XXVII</a>.
The
performance
began
with
Jackson
catapulting
onto
the
stage
as
fireworks
went
off
behind
him.
As
he
landed
on
the
canvas,
he
maintained
a
motionless
&quot;clenched
fist,
standing
statue
stance&quot;,
dressed
in
a
gold
and
black
military
outfit
and
sunglasses;
he
remained
completely
motionless
for
a
minute
and
a
half
while
the
crowd
cheered.
He
then
slowly
removed
his
sunglasses,
threw
them
away
and
sang
four
songs:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Jam_(song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Jam
(song)">Jam</a>&quot;,
&quot;Billie
Jean&quot;,
&quot;Black
or
White&quot;
and
&quot;Heal
the
World&quot;.
It
was
the
first
Super
Bowl
where
the
audience
figures
increased
during
the
half-time
show,
and
was
viewed
by
135&nbsp;million
Americans
alone;
Jackson's
<i>Dangerous</i>
album
rose
90
places
up
the
album
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-campbell_.281995.29_14-16_61-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-campbell_.281995.29_14-16-61">[62]</a></sup>
Jackson
was
given
the
&quot;Living
Legend
Award&quot;
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/35th_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
title="35th
Grammy
Awards">35th
Grammy
Awards</a>
in
Los
Angeles.
&quot;Black
or
White&quot;
was
Grammy-nominated
for
best
vocal
performance.
&quot;Jam&quot;
gained
two
nominations:
Best
R&amp;B
Vocal
Performance
and
Best
R&amp;B
Song.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_45-46_115-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_45-46-115">[116]</a></sup>
The
<i>Dangerous</i>
album
won
a
Grammy
for
Best
Engineered&nbsp;–
Non
Classical,
awarding
the
work
of
Bruce
Swedien
and
Teddy
Riley.
In
the
same
year,
Michael
Jackson
won
three
American
Music
Awards
for
Favorite
Pop/Rock
Album
(<i>Dangerous</i>),
Favorite
Soul/R&amp;B
Single
(&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Remember_the_Time?qsrc=3044"
title="Remember
the
Time">Remember
the
Time</a>&quot;)
and
was
the
first
to
win
the
International
Artist
Award,
for
his
global
performances
and
humanitarian
concerns.
This
award
will
bear
his
name
in
the
future.<sup
id="cite_ref-MJ_Grammy.27s_31-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MJ_Grammy.27s-31">[32]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Bruce_Grammy.27s_38-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Bruce_Grammy.27s-38">[39]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_1993_123-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_1993-123">[124]</a></sup><br
style="clear:both;"
/></p>








<p><span
id="First_child_sexual_abuse_allegations_and_first_marriage_.281993.E2.80.9394.29"></span></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="First_child_sexual_abuse_allegations_and_first_marriage_.281993.E2.80.9394.29">First
child
sexual
abuse
allegations
and
first
marriage
(1993–94)</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/1993_child_sexual_abuse_accusations_against_Michael_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="1993
child
sexual
abuse
accusations
against
Michael
Jackson">1993
child
sexual
abuse
accusations
against
Michael
Jackson</a>







</div>








<p>Jackson
gave
a
90-minute
interview
to
<a
href="/wiki/Oprah_Winfrey?qsrc=3044"
title="Oprah
Winfrey">Oprah
Winfrey</a>
on
February
10,
1993,
his
second
television
interview
since
1979.
He
grimaced
when
speaking
of
his
childhood
abuse
at
the
hands
of
his
father;
he
believed
he
had
missed
out
on
much
of
his
childhood
years,
admitting
that
he
often
cried
from
loneliness.
He
denied
tabloid
rumors
that
he
had
bought
the
bones
of
<a
href="/wiki/Joseph_Merrick?qsrc=3044"
title="Joseph
Merrick">the
Elephant
Man</a>,
slept
in
a
<a
href="/wiki/Hyperbaric?qsrc=3044"
title="Hyperbaric">hyperbaric</a>
oxygen
chamber,
or
bleached
his
skin,
stating
for
the
first
time
that
he
had
<a
href="/wiki/Vitiligo?qsrc=3044"
title="Vitiligo">vitiligo</a>.
<i>Dangerous</i>
re-entered
the
album
chart
in
the
top
10,
more
than
a
year
after
its
original
release.<sup
id="cite_ref-lewis_165-168_15-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lewis_165-168-15">[16]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-campbell_.281995.29_14-16_61-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-campbell_.281995.29_14-16-61">[62]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_45-46_115-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_45-46-115">[116]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
summer
of
1993,
Jackson
was
accused
of
<a
href="/wiki/Child_sexual_abuse?qsrc=3044"
title="Child
sexual
abuse">child
sexual
abuse</a>
by
a
13-year-old
boy
named
Jordan
Chandler
and
his
father,
Dr.
Evan
Chandler,
a
dentist.<sup
id="cite_ref-looking_back_on_1993_124-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-looking_back_on_1993-124">[125]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-tara_485-486_125-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_485-486-125">[126]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-tara_477-478_126-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_477-478-126">[127]</a></sup>
The
Chandler
family
demanded
payment
from
Jackson,
and
the
singer
initially
refused.
Jordan
Chandler
eventually
told
the
police
that
Jackson
had
sexually
abused
him.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_496-498_127-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_496-498-127">[128]</a></sup>
Dr.
Chandler
was
tape-recorded
discussing
his
intention
to
pursue
charges,
saying,
&quot;If
I
go
through
with
this,
I
win
big-time.
There's
no
way
I
lose.
I
will
get
everything
I
want
and
they
will
be
destroyed
forever&nbsp;...
Michael's
career
will
be
over&quot;.
Jordan's
mother
was,
however,
adamant
that
there
had
been
no
wrongdoing
on
Jackson's
part.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_477-478_126-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_477-478-126">[127]</a></sup>
Jackson
later
used
the
recording
to
argue
that
he
was
the
victim
of
a
jealous
father
whose
only
goal
was
to
extort
money
from
the
singer.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_477-478_126-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_477-478-126">[127]</a></sup></p>








<p>Later
that
year,
on
December
20,
Jackson's
home
was
raided
by
the
police,
and
Jackson
submitted
to
a
25-minute
<a
href="/wiki/Strip_search?qsrc=3044"
title="Strip
search">strip
search</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_534-540_128-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_534-540-128">[129]</a></sup>
Jordan
Chandler
had
reportedly
given
police
a
description
of
Jackson's
<a
href="/wiki/Intimate_part?qsrc=3044"
title="Intimate
part">intimate
parts</a>,
notably
claiming
that
his
bleach-damaged
<a
href="/wiki/Human_penis?qsrc=3044"
title="Human
penis">penis</a>
was
<a
href="/wiki/Circumcision?qsrc=3044"
title="Circumcision">circumcised</a>;
the
strip
search
revealed,
to
the
contrary,
that
Jackson
was
actually
<a
href="/wiki/Foreskin?qsrc=3044"
title="Foreskin">uncircumcised</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Never_Recovered_from_1993_Police_Strip_Search_129-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Never_Recovered_from_1993_Police_Strip_Search-129">[130]</a></sup>
a
fact
confirmed
in
his
autopsy.<sup
id="cite_ref-Autopsy_of_Jackson.2C_Michael_Joseph_130-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Autopsy_of_Jackson.2C_Michael_Joseph-130">[131]</a></sup>
His
friends
said
he
never
recovered
from
the
humiliation
of
the
strip
search.
The
investigation
was
inconclusive
and
no
charges
were
ever
filed.<sup
id="cite_ref-Photos_May_Contradict_Michael.27s_Accuser_USA_Today_.28pre-1997_Fulltext.29_.E2.80.93_McLean.2C_Va._Date:_Jan_28.2C_1994_131-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Photos_May_Contradict_Michael.27s_Accuser_USA_Today_.28pre-1997_Fulltext.29_.E2.80.93_McLean.2C_Va._Date:_Jan_28.2C_1994-131">[132]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Photos_May_Contradict_Michael.27s_Accuser_USA_Today_.28pre-1997_Fulltext.29_.E2.80.93_McLean.2C_Va._Date:_Jan_28.2C_199414_132-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Photos_May_Contradict_Michael.27s_Accuser_USA_Today_.28pre-1997_Fulltext.29_.E2.80.93_McLean.2C_Va._Date:_Jan_28.2C_199414-132">[133]</a></sup>
Jackson
described
the
search
in
an
emotional
public
statement,
and
proclaimed
his
innocence.<sup
id="cite_ref-looking_back_on_1993_124-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-looking_back_on_1993-124">[125]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-tara_534-540_128-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_534-540-128">[129]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-campbell_.281995.29_47-50_133-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-campbell_.281995.29_47-50-133">[134]</a></sup>
On
January
1,
1994,
Jackson's
insurance
carrier
settled
with
the
Chandlers
out
of
court
for
$22&nbsp;million.
A
Santa
Barbara
County
grand
jury
and
a
Los
Angeles
County
grand
jury
disbanded
on
May
2,
1994
without
indicting
Jackson.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_Grand_Jury_Disbanded_.E2.80.93_1994._May_2.2C_1994_134-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_Grand_Jury_Disbanded_.E2.80.93_1994._May_2.2C_1994-134">[135]</a></sup>
After
which
time
the
Chandlers
stopped
co-operating
with
the
criminal
investigation
around
July
6,
1994.<sup
id="cite_ref-STATEMENT_OF_DECLINATION_ISSUED_JOINTLY_BY_THE_DISTRICT_ATTORNEY.27S_OFFICES_OF_LOS_ANGELES_AND_SANTA_BARABARA_COUNTIES._September_21.2C_1994_135-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-STATEMENT_OF_DECLINATION_ISSUED_JOINTLY_BY_THE_DISTRICT_ATTORNEY.27S_OFFICES_OF_LOS_ANGELES_AND_SANTA_BARABARA_COUNTIES._September_21.2C_1994-135">[136]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-subpoena-objection_136-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-subpoena-objection-136">[137]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-tara_540-545_137-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_540-545-137">[138]</a></sup>
The
out-of-court
settlement's
documentation
specifically
stated
Jackson
admitted
no
wrongdoing
and
no
liability;
the
Chandlers
and
their
family
lawyer
Larry
Feldman
signed
it
without
contest.<sup
id="cite_ref-thesmokinggun_138-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-thesmokinggun-138">[139]</a></sup>
The
Chandlers'
lawyer
Mr.
Feldman
also
explicitly
stated
&quot;nobody
bought
anybody's
silence&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-latimes_139-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-latimes-139">[140]</a></sup>
A
decade
after
the
fact,
during
the
second
round
of
child
abuse
allegations,
Jackson's
lawyers
would
file
a
memo
stating
that
the
1994
settlement
was
done
without
his
consent.<sup
id="cite_ref-subpoena-objection_136-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-subpoena-objection-136">[137]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
May
1994,
Jackson
married
the
daughter
of
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley?qsrc=3044"
title="Elvis
Presley">Elvis
Presley</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Lisa_Marie_Presley?qsrc=3044"
title="Lisa
Marie
Presley">Lisa
Marie
Presley</a>.
They
had
first
met
in
1975,
when
a
seven-year-old
Presley
attended
one
of
Jackson's
family
engagements
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Hotel_and_Casino?qsrc=3044"
title="MGM
Grand
Hotel
and
Casino">MGM
Grand
Hotel
and
Casino</a>,
and
were
reconnected
through
a
mutual
friend.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_500-507_140-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_500-507-140">[141]</a></sup>
According
to
a
friend
of
Presley's,
&quot;their
adult
friendship
began
in
November
1992
in
L.A.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-gliatto_141-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gliatto-141">[142]</a></sup>
They
stayed
in
contact
every
day
over
the
telephone.
As
the
child
molestation
accusations
became
public,
Jackson
became
dependent
on
Presley
for
emotional
support;
she
was
concerned
about
his
faltering
health
and
addiction
to
drugs.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_518.E2.80.93520_142-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_518.E2.80.93520-142">[143]</a></sup>
Presley
explained,
&quot;I
believed
he
didn't
do
anything
wrong
and
that
he
was
wrongly
accused
and
yes
I
started
falling
for
him.
I
wanted
to
save
him.
I
felt
that
I
could
do
it.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli15_143-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli15-143">[144]</a></sup>
She
eventually
persuaded
him
to
settle
the
allegations
out
of
court
and
go
into
rehabilitation
to
recover.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_518.E2.80.93520_142-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_518.E2.80.93520-142">[143]</a></sup></p>








<p>Jackson
proposed
to
Presley
over
the
telephone
towards
the
fall
of
1993,
saying,
&quot;If
I
asked
you
to
marry
me,
would
you
do
it?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_518.E2.80.93520_142-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_518.E2.80.93520-142">[143]</a></sup>
They
married
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic?qsrc=3044"
title="Dominican
Republic">Dominican
Republic</a>
in
secrecy,
denying
it
for
nearly
two
months
afterwards.<sup
id="cite_ref-MJ_.26_Presley_divorce_144-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MJ_.26_Presley_divorce-144">[145]</a></sup>
The
marriage
was,
in
her
words,
&quot;a
married
couple's
life&nbsp;...
that
was
sexually
active&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli16_145-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli16-145">[146]</a></sup>
At
the
time,
the
tabloid
media
speculated
that
the
wedding
was
a
ploy
to
prop
up
Jackson's
public
image.<sup
id="cite_ref-MJ_.26_Presley_divorce_144-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MJ_.26_Presley_divorce-144">[145]</a></sup>
The
marriage
lasted
less
than
two
years
and
ended
with
an
amicable
divorce
settlement.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_580.E2.80.93581_146-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_580.E2.80.93581-146">[147]</a></sup>
In
a
2010
interview
with
Oprah,
Presley
admitted
that
they
spent
four
more
years
after
the
divorce
&quot;getting
back
together
and
breaking
up&quot;,
until
she
decided
to
stop.<sup
id="cite_ref-lmpoprah_147-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lmpoprah-147">[148]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="HIStory.2C_second_marriage_and_fatherhood_.281995.E2.80.9399.29"><i>HIStory</i>,
second
marriage
and
fatherhood
(1995–99)</span></h3>








<p>In
1995,
Jackson
merged
his
ATV
Music
catalog
with
Sony's
music
publishing
division
creating
<a
href="/wiki/Sony/ATV_Music_Publishing?qsrc=3044"
title="Sony/ATV
Music
Publishing">Sony/ATV
Music
Publishing</a>.
Jackson
retained
half-ownership
of
the
company,
earned
$95&nbsp;million
upfront
as
well
as
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Sony/ATV_Music_Publishing_artists?qsrc=3044"
title="List
of
Sony/ATV
Music
Publishing
artists">the
rights
to
even
more
songs</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-1995_music_deal_148-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-1995_music_deal-148">[149]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-sonydeal_149-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sonydeal-149">[150]</a></sup>
He
then
released
the
double
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/HIStory:_Past,_Present_and_Future,_Book_I?qsrc=3044"
title="HIStory:
Past,
Present
and
Future,
Book
I">HIStory:
Past,
Present
and
Future,
Book&nbsp;I</a></i>.
The
first
disc,
<i>HIStory
Begins</i>,
was
a
15-track
greatest
hits
album,
and
was
later
reissued
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Greatest_Hits:_HIStory,_Volume_I?qsrc=3044"
title="Greatest
Hits:
HIStory,
Volume
I">Greatest
Hits:
HIStory,
Volume
I</a></i>
in
2001,
while
the
second
disc,
<i>HIStory
Continues</i>,
contained
15
new
songs.
The
album
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
charts
and
has
been
certified
for
seven&nbsp;million
shipments
in
the
US.<sup
id="cite_ref-Top_100_Albums_.28Page_2.29_150-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Top_100_Albums_.28Page_2.29-150">[151]</a></sup>
It
is
the
best-selling
multiple-disc
album
of
all-time,
with
20&nbsp;million
copies
(40&nbsp;million
units)
sold
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_achievements_114-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_achievements-114">[115]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-HIStory_.7B.7BNowrap.7C20_million.7D.7D_copies_151-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-HIStory_.7B.7BNowrap.7C20_million.7D.7D_copies-151">[152]</a></sup>
<i>HIStory</i>
received
a
Grammy
nomination
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Album
of
the
Year">Album
of
the
Year</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup></p>








<p>&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Scream/Childhood?qsrc=3044"
title="Scream/Childhood">Scream/Childhood</a>&quot;.
&quot;Scream&quot;
was
a
duet,
performed
with
Jackson's
youngest
sister
<a
href="/wiki/Janet_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="Janet
Jackson">Janet</a>.
The
song
fights
against
the
media,
mainly
for
what
the
media
made
him
out
to
be
during
his
1993
child
abuse
allegations.
The
single
had
the
highest
debut
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>&nbsp;Hot&nbsp;100
at
number
five,
and
received
a
Grammy
nomination
for
&quot;Best
Pop
Collaboration
with
Vocals&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Are_Not_Alone?qsrc=3044"
title="You
Are
Not
Alone">You
Are
Not
Alone</a>&quot;
was
the
second
single
released
from
<i>HIStory</i>;
it
holds
the
<i>Guinness
World
Record</i>
for
the
first
song
ever
to
debut
at
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>&nbsp;Hot&nbsp;100
chart.<sup
id="cite_ref-World_Records_100-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-World_Records-100">[101]</a></sup>
It
was
seen
as
a
major
artistic
and
commercial
success,
receiving
a
Grammy
nomination
for
&quot;Best
Pop
Vocal
Performance&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup>
In
late
1995,
Jackson
was
rushed
to
a
hospital
after
collapsing
during
rehearsals
for
a
televised
performance;
the
incident
was
caused
by
a
stress-related
<a
href="/wiki/Panic_attack?qsrc=3044"
title="Panic
attack">panic
attack</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli17_153-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli17-153">[154]</a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Earth_Song?qsrc=3044"
title="Earth
Song">Earth
Song</a>&quot;
was
the
third
single
released
from
<i>HIStory</i>,
and
topped
the
<a
href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart?qsrc=3044"
title="UK
Singles
Chart">UK
Singles
Chart</a>
for
six
weeks
over
Christmas
1995;
it
sold
a
million
copies,
making
it
Jackson's
most
successful
single
in
the
UK.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup>
The
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/They_Don%27t_Care_About_Us?qsrc=3044"
title="They
Don't
Care
About
Us">They
Don't
Care
About
Us</a>&quot;
became
controversial
when
the
<a
href="/wiki/Anti-Defamation_League?qsrc=3044"
title="Anti-Defamation
League">Anti-Defamation
League</a>
and
other
groups
criticized
its
allegedly
<a
href="/wiki/Antisemitism?qsrc=3044"
title="Antisemitism">antisemitic</a>
lyrics.
Jackson
quickly
put
out
a
revised
version
of
the
song
without
the
offending
lyrics.<sup
id="cite_ref-ADL_154-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ADL-154">[155]</a></sup>
In
1996,
Jackson
won
a
Grammy
for
Best
Music
Video,
Short
Form
for
&quot;Scream&quot;
and
an
American
Music
Award
for
Favorite
Pop/Rock
Male
Artist.<sup
id="cite_ref-MJ_Grammy.27s_31-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MJ_Grammy.27s-31">[32]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_1996_155-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_1996-155">[156]</a></sup></p>








<p>The
album
was
promoted
with
the
successful
<a
href="/wiki/HIStory_World_Tour?qsrc=3044"
title="HIStory
World
Tour">HIStory
World
Tour</a>.
The
tour
began
on
September
7,
1996,
and
finished
on
October
15,
1997.
Jackson
performed
82
concerts
in
58
cities
to
over
4.5&nbsp;million
fans,
and
grossed
a
total
of
<span
class="nowrap">$165
million</span>.
The
show,
which
visited
five
continents
and
35
countries,
became
Jackson's
most
successful
in
terms
of
audience
figures.<sup
id="cite_ref-lewis_95-96_92-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lewis_95-96-92">[93]</a></sup>
During
the
tour,
Jackson
married
his
<a
href="/wiki/Personal_relationships_of_Michael_Jackson?qsrc=3044#Debbie_Rowe"
title="Personal
relationships
of
Michael
Jackson">longtime
friend</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Debbie_Rowe?qsrc=3044"
title="Debbie
Rowe">Deborah
Jeanne
Rowe</a>,
a
dermatology
nurse,
in
an
impromptu
ceremony
in
Sydney,
Australia.
Rowe
was
approximately
six
months
pregnant
with
the
couple's
first
child
at
the
time.
Originally,
Rowe
and
Jackson
had
no
plans
to
marry,
but
Jackson's
mother
Katherine
persuaded
them
to
do
so.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli18_156-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli18-156">[157]</a></sup>
Michael
Joseph
Jackson
Jr
(commonly
known
as
Prince)
was
born
on
February
13,
1997;
his
sister
Paris-Michael
Katherine
Jackson
was
born
a
year
later
on
April
3,
1998.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_580.E2.80.93581_146-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_580.E2.80.93581-146">[147]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli19_157-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli19-157">[158]</a></sup>
The
couple
divorced
in
1999,
and
Jackson
got
full
custody
of
the
children.
The
divorce
was
relatively
amicable,
but
a
subsequent
custody
suit
was
not
settled
until
2006.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_599-600_158-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_599-600-158">[159]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_settles_with_Ex_wife_159-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_settles_with_Ex_wife-159">[160]</a></sup></p>

<p>In
1997,
Jackson
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Blood_on_the_Dance_Floor:_HIStory_in_the_Mix?qsrc=3044"
title="Blood
on
the
Dance
Floor:
HIStory
in
the
Mix">Blood
on
the
Dance
Floor:
HIStory
in
the
Mix</a></i>,
which
contained
remixes
of
hit
singles
from
<i>HIStory</i>
and
five
new
songs.
Worldwide
sales
stand
at
<span
class="nowrap">6
million</span>
copies
as
of
2007,
it
is
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_remix_albums_worldwide?qsrc=3044"
title="List
of
best-selling
remix
albums
worldwide">best
selling
remix
album
ever
released</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rojek2007_160-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rojek2007-160">[161]</a></sup>
It
reached
number
one
in
the
UK,
as
did
the
<a
href="/wiki/Blood_on_the_Dance_Floor_(song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Blood
on
the
Dance
Floor
(song)">title
track</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rojek2007_160-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rojek2007-160">[161]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-tara_610.E2.80.93611_161-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_610.E2.80.93611-161">[162]</a></sup>
In
the
US,
the
album
was
certified
platinum,
but
only
reached
number
24.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_certifications_111-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA_certifications-111">[112]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup>
Forbes
placed
his
annual
income
at
$35&nbsp;million
in
1996
and
$20&nbsp;million
in
1997.<sup
id="cite_ref-usatoday_finances_99-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-usatoday_finances-99">[100]</a></sup>
Throughout
June
1999,
Jackson
was
involved
in
a
number
of
charitable
events.
He
joined
<a
href="/wiki/Luciano_Pavarotti?qsrc=3044"
title="Luciano
Pavarotti">Luciano
Pavarotti</a>
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/Benefit_concert?qsrc=3044"
title="Benefit
concert">benefit
concert</a>
in
Modena,
Italy.
The
show
was
in
support
of
the
nonprofit
organization
<a
href="/wiki/War_Child_(charity)?qsrc=3044"
title="War
Child
(charity)">War
Child</a>,
and
raised
a
million
dollars
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/1999_NATO_bombing_of_Yugoslavia?qsrc=3044"
title="1999
NATO
bombing
of
Yugoslavia">refugees
of
Kosovo,
FR
Yugoslavia</a>,
as
well
as
additional
funds
for
the
children
of
Guatemala.<sup
id="cite_ref-Charity_concert_Italy_162-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Charity_concert_Italy-162">[163]</a></sup>
Later
that
month,
Jackson
organized
a
set
of
&quot;Michael
Jackson
&amp;
Friends&quot;
benefit
concerts
in
Germany
and
Korea.
Other
artists
involved
included
<a
href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
title="Slash
(musician)">Slash</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Scorpions_(band)?qsrc=3044"
title="Scorpions
(band)">The
Scorpions</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Boyz_II_Men?qsrc=3044"
title="Boyz
II
Men">Boyz
II
Men</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Luther_Vandross?qsrc=3044"
title="Luther
Vandross">Luther
Vandross</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey?qsrc=3044"
title="Mariah
Carey">Mariah
Carey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/A._R._Rahman?qsrc=3044"
title="A.
R.
Rahman">A.
R.
Rahman</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Prabhu_Deva?qsrc=3044"
title="Prabhu
Deva">Prabhu
Deva
Sundaram</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Shobana?qsrc=3044"
title="Shobana">Shobana</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Andrea_Bocelli?qsrc=3044"
title="Andrea
Bocelli">Andrea
Bocelli</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Luciano_Pavarotti?qsrc=3044"
title="Luciano
Pavarotti">Luciano
Pavarotti</a>.
The
proceeds
went
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Nelson_Mandela_Children%27s_Fund?qsrc=3044"
title="Nelson
Mandela
Children's
Fund">Nelson
Mandela
Children's
Fund</a>,
the
<a
href="/wiki/International_Red_Cross_and_Red_Crescent_Movement?qsrc=3044"
title="International
Red
Cross
and
Red
Crescent
Movement">Red
Cross</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/UNESCO?qsrc=3044"
title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_.26_Friends_163-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_.26_Friends-163">[164]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Label_dispute.2C_Invincible_and_third_child_.282000.E2.80.9303.29">Label
dispute,
<i>Invincible</i>
and
third
child
(2000–03)</span></h3>








<p>At
the
turn
of
the
century,
Jackson
won
an
American
Music
Award
as
Artist
of
the
1980s.<sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_Poll_164-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_Poll-164">[165]</a></sup>
Throughout
2000
and
2001,
Jackson
worked
in
the
studio
with
Teddy
Riley
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rodney_Jerkins?qsrc=3044"
title="Rodney
Jerkins">Rodney
Jerkins</a>,
as
well
as
other
collaborators.
These
sessions
would
result
in
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Invincible_(Michael_Jackson_album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Invincible
(Michael
Jackson
album)">Invincible</a></i>,
released
in
October
2001.
<i>Invincible</i>
was
Jackson's
first
full-length
album
in
six
years,
and
it
would
be
the
last
album
of
new
material
he
released
while
still
alive.
The
release
of
the
album
was
preceded
by
a
dispute
between
Jackson
and
his
record
label,
<a
href="/wiki/Sony_Music_Entertainment?qsrc=3044"
title="Sony
Music
Entertainment">Sony
Music
Entertainment</a>.
Jackson
had
expected
the
licenses
to
the
masters
of
his
albums
to
revert
to
him
sometime
in
the
early
2000s.
Once
he
had
the
licenses,
he
would
be
able
to
promote
the
material
however
he
pleased
and
keep
all
the
profits.
However,
due
to
various
clauses
in
the
contract,
the
revert
date
turned
out
to
be
many
years
away.
Jackson
discovered
that
the
attorney
who
represented
him
in
the
deal
was
also
representing
Sony.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_610.E2.80.93611_161-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_610.E2.80.93611-161">[162]</a></sup>
Jackson
was
also
concerned
about
the
fact
that
for
a
number
of
years,
Sony
had
been
pressuring
him
to
sell
his
share
in
their
music
catalog
venture.
Jackson
feared
that
Sony
might
have
a
conflict
of
interest,
since
if
Jackson's
career
failed,
he
would
have
to
sell
his
share
of
the
catalog
at
a
low
price.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_614.E2.80.93617_165-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_614.E2.80.93617-165">[166]</a></sup>
Jackson
sought
an
early
exit
from
his
contract.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_610.E2.80.93611_161-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_610.E2.80.93611-161">[162]</a></sup>
Just
before
the
release
of
<i>Invincible</i>,
Jackson
informed
the
head
of
Sony
Music
Entertainment,
<a
href="/wiki/Tommy_Mottola?qsrc=3044"
title="Tommy
Mottola">Tommy
Mottola</a>,
that
he
was
leaving
Sony.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_610.E2.80.93611_161-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_610.E2.80.93611-161">[162]</a></sup>
As
a
result,
all
singles
releases,
video
shootings
and
promotions
concerning
the
<i>Invincible</i>
album
were
suspended.</p>








<p>In
September
2001,
two
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson:_30th_Anniversary_Special?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson:
30th
Anniversary
Special">30th
Anniversary
concerts</a>
were
held
at
Madison
Square
Garden
to
mark
the
singer's
30th
year
as
a
solo
artist.
Jackson
appeared
onstage
alongside
his
brothers
for
the
first
time
since
1984.
The
show
also
featured
performances
by
<a
href="/wiki/M%C3%BDa?qsrc=3044"
title="M&yacute;a">M&yacute;a</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
title="Usher
(entertainer)">Usher</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Whitney_Houston?qsrc=3044"
title="Whitney
Houston">Whitney
Houston</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/%27N_Sync?qsrc=3044"
title="'N
Sync">'N
Sync</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Destiny%27s_Child?qsrc=3044"
title="Destiny's
Child">Destiny's
Child</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Monica_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
title="Monica
(entertainer)">Monica</a>,
Luther
Vandross,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Slash_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
title="Slash
(musician)">Slash</a>,
among
other
artists.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_50-53_166-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_50-53-166">[167]</a></sup>
The
second
of
the
two
shows
took
place
the
night
before
the
<a
href="/wiki/September_11_attacks?qsrc=3044"
title="September
11
attacks">September
11,
2001,
terrorist
attacks</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-guardian_167-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guardian-167">[168]</a></sup>
After
9/11,
Jackson
helped
organize
the
<a
href="/wiki/United_We_Stand:_What_More_Can_I_Give?qsrc=3044"
title="United
We
Stand:
What
More
Can
I
Give">United
We
Stand:
What
More
Can
I
Give</a>
benefit
concert
at
<a
href="/wiki/Robert_F._Kennedy_Memorial_Stadium?qsrc=3044"
title="Robert
F.
Kennedy
Memorial
Stadium">RFK
Stadium</a>
in
Washington,
D.C.
The
concert
took
place
on
October
21,
2001,
and
included
performances
from
dozens
of
major
artists,
including
Jackson,
who
performed
his
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/What_More_Can_I_Give?qsrc=3044"
title="What
More
Can
I
Give">What
More
Can
I
Give</a>&quot;
as
the
finale.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_614.E2.80.93617_165-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_614.E2.80.93617-165">[166]</a></sup>
Jackson's
solo
performances
were
omitted
from
the
televised
version
of
the
benefit
concert,
although
he
could
still
be
seen
singing
background
vocals.
This
omission
happened
because
of
contractual
issues
related
to
the
earlier
30th
Anniversary
concerts:
those
concerts
were
boiled
down
into
a
two-hour
TV
special
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson:_30th_Anniversary_Special?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson:
30th
Anniversary
Special">Michael
Jackson:
30th
Anniversary
Celebration</a></i>
which
debuted
in
November
2001.</p>








<p>In
spite
of
the
events
preceding
its
release,
<i>Invincible</i>
came
out
in
October
2001
to
much
anticipation.
<i>Invincible</i>
proved
to
be
a
hit,
debuting
atop
the
charts
in
13
countries
and
going
on
to
sell
approximately
13&nbsp;million
copies
worldwide.
It
received
double-platinum
certification
in
the
U.S.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_certifications_111-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA_certifications-111">[112]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_achievements_114-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_achievements-114">[115]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Invincible_.7B.7BNowrap.7C13_million.7D.7D_copies_168-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Invincible_.7B.7BNowrap.7C13_million.7D.7D_copies-168">[169]</a></sup>
However,
the
sales
for
<i>Invincible</i>
were
lower
than
those
of
his
previous
releases,
due
in
part
to
a
lack
of
promotion,
no
supporting
world
tour
and
the
label
dispute.
The
album
also
came
out
at
a
bad
time
for
the
music
industry
in
general.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_614.E2.80.93617_165-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_614.E2.80.93617-165">[166]</a></sup>
The
album
cost
<span
class="nowrap">$30
million</span>
to
record,
not
including
promotional
expenditures.<sup
id="cite_ref-guardian-February_7.2C_2008_169-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guardian-February_7.2C_2008-169">[170]</a></sup>
<i>Invincible</i>
spawned
three
singles,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Rock_My_World?qsrc=3044"
title="You
Rock
My
World">You
Rock
My
World</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cry_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Cry
(Michael
Jackson
song)">Cry</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Butterflies_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Butterflies
(Michael
Jackson
song)">Butterflies</a>&quot;,
the
latter
without
a
music
video.
Jackson
alleged
in
July
2002
that
Mottola
was
a
&quot;devil&quot;
and
a
&quot;racist&quot;
who
did
not
support
his
African-American
artists,
using
them
merely
for
his
own
personal
gain.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_614.E2.80.93617_165-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_614.E2.80.93617-165">[166]</a></sup>
He
charged
that
Mottola
had
called
his
colleague
<a
href="/wiki/Irv_Gotti?qsrc=3044"
title="Irv
Gotti">Irv
Gotti</a>
a
&quot;fat
<a
href="/wiki/Nigger?qsrc=3044"
title="Nigger">nigger</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Interview_with_Jermaine_Jackson_170-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Interview_with_Jermaine_Jackson-170">[171]</a></sup>
Sony
refused
to
renew
Jackson's
contract,
and
claimed
that
a
<span
class="nowrap">$25
million</span>
promotional
campaign
had
failed
because
Jackson
refused
to
tour
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-guardian-February_7.2C_2008_169-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guardian-February_7.2C_2008-169">[170]</a></sup></p>








<p><span
id="Blanket_Jackson"></span>
In
2002,
Michael
Jackson
won
his
22nd
American
Music
Award
for
Artist
of
the
Century.<sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_2002_171-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_2002-171">[172]</a></sup>
In
the
same
year,
Jackson's
third
child,
Prince
Michael
Jackson&nbsp;II
(nicknamed
&quot;Blanket&quot;)
was
born.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_172-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson-172">[173]</a></sup>
The
mother's
identity
is
unknown,
but
Jackson
has
said
the
child
was
the
result
of
<a
href="/wiki/Artificial_insemination?qsrc=3044"
title="Artificial
insemination">artificial
insemination</a>
from
a
<a
href="/wiki/Surrogacy?qsrc=3044"
title="Surrogacy">surrogate
mother</a>
and
his
own
sperm.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_599-600_158-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_599-600-158">[159]</a></sup>
On
November
20
of
that
year,
Jackson
brought
his
newborn
son
onto
the
balcony
of
his
room
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hotel_Adlon?qsrc=3044"
title="Hotel
Adlon">Hotel
Adlon</a>
in
Berlin,
as
fans
stood
below,
holding
him
in
his
right
arm,
with
a
cloth
loosely
draped
over
the
baby's
face.
The
baby
was
briefly
extended
over
a
railing,
four
stories
above
ground
level,
causing
widespread
criticism
in
the
media.
Jackson
later
apologized
for
the
incident,
calling
it
&quot;a
terrible
mistake&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Balcony_incident_173-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Balcony_incident-173">[174]</a></sup>
Sony
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Number_Ones_(Michael_Jackson_album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Number
Ones
(Michael
Jackson
album)">Number
Ones</a></i>,
a
compilation
of
Jackson's
hits
on
CD
and
DVD.
In
the
U.S.,
the
album
was
certified
triple
platinum
by
the
RIAA;
in
the
UK
it
was
certified
six
times
platinum
for
shipments
of
at
least
<span
class="nowrap">1.2
million</span>
units.<sup
id="cite_ref-RIAA_certifications_111-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RIAA_certifications-111">[112]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-BPI_174-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-BPI-174">[175]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Second_child_sexual_abuse_allegations_and_acquittal_.282003.E2.80.9305.29">Second
child
sexual
abuse
allegations
and
acquittal
(2003–05)</span></h3>








<div
class="rellink">








Further
information:









<a
href="/wiki/Living_with_Michael_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="Living
with
Michael
Jackson">Living
with
Michael
Jackson</a>&nbsp;and&nbsp;








<a
href="/wiki/People_v._Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="People
v.
Jackson">People
v.
Jackson</a>







</div>








<p>Beginning
in
May
2002,
Jackson
allowed
a
documentary
film
crew,
led
by
British
TV
personality
<a
href="/wiki/Martin_Bashir?qsrc=3044"
title="Martin
Bashir">Martin
Bashir</a>,
to
follow
him
around
just
about
everywhere
he
went.
Bashir's
film
crew
was
with
Jackson
during
the
&quot;baby-dangling
incident&quot;
in
Berlin.
The
program
was
broadcast
in
March
2003
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Living_with_Michael_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="Living
with
Michael
Jackson">Living
with
Michael
Jackson</a></i>,
and
painted
an
extraordinarily
unflattering
portrait
of
the
singer.</p>








<p>In
a
particularly
controversial
scene,
Jackson
was
seen
holding
hands
and
discussing
sleeping
arrangements
with
a
young
boy.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_640_175-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_640-175">[176]</a></sup>
As
soon
as
the
documentary
aired,
the
Santa
Barbara
county
attorney's
office
began
a
criminal
investigation.
Jackson
was
arrested
in
November
2003,
and
was
charged
with
seven
counts
of
child
molestation
and
two
counts
of
<a
href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage?qsrc=3044#United_States_of_America"
title="Alcoholic
beverage">administering
an
intoxicating
agent</a>
in
relation
to
the
13-year
old
boy
shown
in
the
film.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_640_175-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_640-175">[176]</a></sup>
Jackson
denied
the
allegations,
saying
the
sleepovers
were
not
sexual
in
nature.
The
<i><a
href="/wiki/People_v._Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="People
v.
Jackson">People
v.
Jackson</a></i>
trial
began
on
January
31,
2005,
in
<a
href="/wiki/Santa_Maria,_California?qsrc=3044"
title="Santa
Maria,
California">Santa
Maria</a>,
California,
and
lasted
five
months,
until
the
end
of
May.
On
June
13,
2005,
Jackson
was
acquitted
on
all
counts.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli20_176-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli20-176">[177]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_health_concerns_177-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_health_concerns-177">[178]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_jury_reaches_verdict_178-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_jury_reaches_verdict-178">[179]</a></sup>
After
the
trial,
in
a
highly
publicized
relocation
he
moved
to
the
Persian
Gulf
island
of
<a
href="/wiki/Bahrain?qsrc=3044"
title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>,
as
a
guest
of
<a
href="/wiki/Abdullah_Bin_Hamad_Bin_Isa_Al-Khalifa?qsrc=3044"
title="Abdullah
Bin
Hamad
Bin
Isa
Al-Khalifa">Sheikh
Abdullah</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_settles_down_to_his_new_life_in_the_Persian_Gulf_179-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_settles_down_to_his_new_life_in_the_Persian_Gulf-179">[180]</a></sup>
Bahrain
was
also
where
the
family
intended
to
send
Jackson
if
he
was
convicted
(though
Jackson
did
not
know
about
the
plan),
according
to
a
statement
by
Jermaine
Jackson
printed
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Times?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Times">The
Times</a></i>
of
London
in
September
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jermaine_Jackson_reveals_escape_plan_for_Michael_180-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jermaine_Jackson_reveals_escape_plan_for_Michael-180">[181]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Closure_of_Neverland.2C_final_years_and_This_Is_It_.282006.E2.80.9309.29">Closure
of

and
<i>This
Is
It</i>
(2006–09)<span

<div

Jackson

in

2006









</div>

<p>In
March
2006,
the
main
house
at
the
Neverland
Ranch
was
closed
as
a
cost-cutting
measure.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_Closes_Neverland_House_181-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_Closes_Neverland_House-181">[182]</a></sup>
There
were
numerous
reports
around
that
time
that
Jackson
was
having
financial
problems.
Jackson
had
been
delinquent
on
his
repayments
of
a
$270&nbsp;million
loan
secured
against
his
music
publishing
holdings,
even
though
those
holdings
were
reportedly
making
him
as
much
as
<span
class="nowrap">$75
million</span>
a
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-Really_Odd_Facts_About_Michael_Jackson_182-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Really_Odd_Facts_About_Michael_Jackson-182">[183]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Bank_of_America?qsrc=3044"
title="Bank
of
America">Bank
of
America</a>
sold
the
debt
to
<a
href="/wiki/Fortress_Investment_Group?qsrc=3044"
title="Fortress
Investment
Group">Fortress
Investments</a>.
Sony
reportedly
proposed
a
restructuring
deal
which
would
give
them
a
future
option
to
buy
half
of
Jackson's
stake
in
their
jointly
owned
publishing
company
(leaving
Jackson
with
a
25%
stake).<sup
id="cite_ref-sonydeal_149-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-sonydeal-149">[150]</a></sup>
Jackson
agreed
to
a
Sony-backed
refinancing
deal
in
April
2006,
although
the
exact
details
were
not
made
public.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_strikes_deal_over_loans_183-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_strikes_deal_over_loans-183">[184]</a></sup>
Jackson
did
not
have
a
recording
contract
in
place
with
Sony
or
any
other
major
record
label
at
the
time.</p>








<p>In
early
2006,
there
was
an
announcement
that
Jackson
had
signed
a
contract
with
a
<a
href="/wiki/Bahrain?qsrc=3044"
title="Bahrain">Bahrain</a>-based
startup
called
Two
Seas
Records.
However,
nothing
ever
came
of
that
deal,
and
the
CEO
of
Two
Seas,
<a
href="/wiki/Gut_Records?qsrc=3044"
title="Gut
Records">Guy
Holmes</a>,
later
stated
that
the
deal
had
never
been
finalized.<sup
id="cite_ref-2seas-billboard_184-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2seas-billboard-184">[185]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-2seas-bbc_185-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2seas-bbc-185">[186]</a></sup>
Throughout
2006,
Sony
repackaged
20
singles
from
the
1980s
and
1990s
as
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Visionary:_The_Video_Singles?qsrc=3044"
title="Visionary:
The
Video
Singles">Michael
Jackson:
Visionary</a></i>
series,
which
subsequently
became
a
<a
href="/wiki/Box_set?qsrc=3044"
title="Box
set">box
set</a>.
Most
of
those
singles
returned
to
the
charts
as
a
result.
In
September
2006,
Jackson
and
his
ex-wife
Debbie
Rowe
confirmed
reports
that
they
had
settled
their
long-running
child
custody
suit.
The
terms
were
never
made
public.
Jackson
continued
to
be
the
custodial
parent
of
the
couple's
two
children.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_settles_with_Ex_wife_159-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_settles_with_Ex_wife-159">[160]</a></sup>
In
October
2006,
<a
href="/wiki/Fox_News?qsrc=3044"
title="Fox
News">Fox
News</a>
entertainment
reporter
Roger
Friedman
said
that
Jackson
had
been
recording
at
a
studio
in
rural
<a
href="/wiki/County_Westmeath?qsrc=3044"
title="County
Westmeath">Westmeath,
Ireland</a>.
It
was
not
known
at
the
time
what
Jackson
might
be
working
on,
or
who
might
be
paying
for
the
sessions,
since
his
publicist
had
recently
issued
a
statement
claiming
that
he
had
left
Two
Seas.<sup
id="cite_ref-2seas-bbc_185-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2seas-bbc-185">[186]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Who.27s_Funding_Jackson.27s_Retreat_to_Irish_Recording_Studio.3F_186-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Who.27s_Funding_Jackson.27s_Retreat_to_Irish_Recording_Studio.3F-186">[187]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
November
2006,
Jackson
invited
an
<i><a
href="/wiki/Access_Hollywood?qsrc=3044"
title="Access
Hollywood">Access
Hollywood</a></i>
camera
crew
into
the
studio
in
Westmeath,
and
<a
href="/wiki/MSNBC?qsrc=3044"
title="MSNBC">MSNBC</a>
broke
the
story
that
he
was
working
on
a
new
album,
produced
by
<a
href="/wiki/Will.i.am?qsrc=3044"
title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Black_Eyed_Peas?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Black
Eyed
Peas">The
Black
Eyed
Peas</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_achievements_114-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_achievements-114">[115]</a></sup>
Jackson
performed
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/2006_World_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
title="2006
World
Music
Awards">World
Music
Awards</a>,
in
London
on
November
15,
2006,
and
accepted
a
Diamond
Award
for
selling
over
<span
class="nowrap">100
million</span>
records.<sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_achievements_114-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_achievements-114">[115]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-2006_World_Music_Awards_187-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2006_World_Music_Awards-187">[188]</a></sup>
Jackson
returned
to
the
United
States
after
Christmas
2006
to
attend
<a
href="/wiki/James_Brown?qsrc=3044"
title="James
Brown">James
Brown</a>'s
funeral
in
<a
href="/wiki/Augusta,_Georgia?qsrc=3044"
title="Augusta,
Georgia">Augusta</a>,
Georgia.
He
gave
one
of
the
eulogies,
saying
that
&quot;James
Brown
is
my
greatest
inspiration.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-jb_188-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-jb-188">[189]</a></sup>
In
the
spring
of
2007,
Jackson
and
Sony
teamed
up
to
buy
yet
another
music
publishing
company:
<a
href="/wiki/Famous_Music?qsrc=3044"
title="Famous
Music">Famous
Music
LLC</a>,
formerly
owned
by
<a
href="/wiki/Viacom?qsrc=3044"
title="Viacom">Viacom</a>.
This
deal
gave
him
the
rights
to
songs
by
<a
href="/wiki/Eminem?qsrc=3044"
title="Eminem">Eminem</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Shakira?qsrc=3044"
title="Shakira">Shakira</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Beck?qsrc=3044"
title="Beck">Beck</a>,
among
others.<sup
id="cite_ref-2007_music_deal_189-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2007_music_deal-189">[190]</a></sup>
Jackson
recorded
extensively
during
this
period
in
New
York
with
songwriter
and
producer
will.i.am
and
also
in
Las
Vegas
with
producers
<a
href="/wiki/Akon?qsrc=3044"
title="Akon">Akon</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/RedOne?qsrc=3044"
title="RedOne">RedOne</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-telegraph-june09_190-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-telegraph-june09-190">[191]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-hitquarters.com_191-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hitquarters.com-191">[192]</a></sup>
In
March
2007,
Jackson
gave
a
brief
interview
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Associated_Press?qsrc=3044"
title="Associated
Press">Associated
Press</a>
in
Tokyo,
where
he
said,
&quot;I've
been
in
the
entertainment
industry
since
I
was
6
years
old,
and
as
<a
href="/wiki/Charles_Dickens?qsrc=3044"
title="Charles
Dickens">Charles
Dickens</a>
would
say,
'It's
been
the
best
of
times,
the
worst
of
times.'
But
I
would
not
change
my
career&nbsp;...
While
some
have
made
deliberate
attempts
to
hurt
me,
I
take
it
in
stride
because
I
have
a
loving
family,
a
strong
faith
and
wonderful
friends
and
fans
who
have,
and
continue,
to
support
me.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-usatoday_192-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-usatoday-192">[193]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
September
2007,
Jackson
was
reportedly
still
working
with
will.i.am,
but
the
album
was
apparently
never
completed.<sup
id="cite_ref-Will.i.am_On_Working_With_Michael_Jackson_193-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Will.i.am_On_Working_With_Michael_Jackson-193">[194]</a></sup>
However,
in
2008,
Jackson
and
Sony
released
<i><a
href="/wiki/Thriller_25?qsrc=3044"
title="Thriller
25">Thriller
25</a></i>
to
mark
the
25th
anniversary
of
the
original
<i><a
href="/wiki/Thriller_(album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Thriller
(album)">Thriller</a></i>.
This
album
featured
the
previously
unreleased
song
&quot;For
All
Time&quot;
(an
outtake
from
the
original
sessions)
as
well
as
remixes,
where
Jackson
collaborated
with
younger
artists
who
had
been
inspired
by
his
work.<sup
id="cite_ref-National_certifications_for_Thriller_25_194-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-National_certifications_for_Thriller_25-194">[195]</a></sup>
Two
of
the
remixes
were
released
as
singles
with
only
modest
success:
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Girl_Is_Mine_2008?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Girl
Is
Mine
2008">The
Girl
Is
Mine
2008</a>&quot;
(with
<a
href="/wiki/Will.i.am?qsrc=3044"
title="Will.i.am">will.i.am</a>)
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wanna_Be_Startin%27_Somethin%27_2008?qsrc=3044"
title="Wanna
Be
Startin'
Somethin'
2008">Wanna
Be
Startin'
Somethin'
2008</a>&quot;
(with
<a
href="/wiki/Akon?qsrc=3044"
title="Akon">Akon</a>).
The
first
single
was
based
on
an
early
demo
version,
without
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_McCartney?qsrc=3044"
title="Paul
McCartney">Paul
McCartney</a>.
The
album
itself
was
a
hit,
however.<sup
id="cite_ref-National_certifications_for_Thriller_25_194-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-National_certifications_for_Thriller_25-194">[195]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Thriller_25_chart_positions_at_digitalproducer_195-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Thriller_25_chart_positions_at_digitalproducer-195">[196]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Thriller_25_chart_positions_196-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Thriller_25_chart_positions-196">[197]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Worldwide_shipments_of_T25_197-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Worldwide_shipments_of_T25-197">[198]</a></sup>
In
anticipation
of
Jackson's
50th&nbsp;birthday,
Sony
BMG
released
a
series
of
greatest-hits
albums
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/King_of_Pop_(album)?qsrc=3044"
title="King
of
Pop
(album)">King
of
Pop</a></i>.
Slightly
different
versions
were
released
in
various
countries,
based
on
polls
of
local
fans.<sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_announced_198-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_announced-198">[199]</a></sup>
<i>King
of
Pop</i>
reached
the
top
10
in
most
countries
where
it
was
issued,
and
also
sold
well
as
an
import
in
other
countries
(such
as
the
United
States.)<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson.E2.80.94King_of_Pop_199-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson.E2.80.94King_of_Pop-199">[200]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_chart_positions_at_ultratop_200-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_chart_positions_at_ultratop-200">[201]</a></sup></p>

tleft">

<div

An
aerial
view
of
part
of
Jackson's
2,800
acre
Neverland

Ranch
near
Los
Olivos,
CA
showing
the
many
rides









</div>

<p>In
late
2008,
Fortress
Investments
threatened
to
foreclose
on
<a
href="/wiki/Neverland_Ranch?qsrc=3044"
title="Neverland
Ranch">Neverland
Ranch</a>,
which
Jackson
used
as
collateral
for
loans
running
into
many
tens
of
millions
of
dollars.
However,
Fortress
opted
to
sell
Jackson's
debts
to
<a
href="/wiki/Colony_Capital?qsrc=3044"
title="Colony
Capital">Colony
Capital
LLC</a>.
In
November,
Jackson
transferred
Neverland
Ranch's
title
to
Sycamore
Valley
Ranch
Company
LLC,
which
was
a
joint
venture
between
Jackson
and
Colony
Capital
LLC.
This
deal
cleared
Jackson's
debt,
and
he
reportedly
even
gained
an
extra
<span
class="nowrap">$35
million</span>
from
the
venture.
At
the
time
of
his
death,
Jackson
still
owned
a
stake
in
Neverland/Sycamore
Valley,
but
it
is
unknown
how
large
that
stake
was.<sup
id="cite_ref-Neverland_peters_out_for_pop.27s_Peter_Pan_201-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Neverland_peters_out_for_pop.27s_Peter_Pan-201">[202]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-association_202-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-association-202">[203]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Ten_Most_Expensive_Michael_Jackson_Collectibles_203-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ten_Most_Expensive_Michael_Jackson_Collectibles-203">[204]</a></sup>
In
September
2008,
Jackson
entered
negotiations
with
<a
href="/wiki/Julien%27s_Auctions?qsrc=3044"
title="Julien's
Auctions">Julien's
Auction
House</a>
to
display
and
auction
a
large
collection
of
memorabilia
amounting
to
approximately
1,390
lots.
The
auction
was
scheduled
to
take
place
between
April
22
and
25.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Exhibition.C2.A0.E2.80.93_2009_204-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Exhibition.C2.A0.E2.80.93_2009-204">[205]</a></sup>
An
exhibition
of
the
lots
opened
as
scheduled
on
April
14,
but
the
actual
auction
was
eventually
cancelled
at
Jackson's
request.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson:_The_fantastic_possessions_revealed.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Americas.2C_World_205-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson:_The_fantastic_possessions_revealed.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Americas.2C_World-205">[206]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
March
2009,
Jackson
held
a
press
conference
at
London's
<a
href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)?qsrc=3044"
title="The
O2
Arena
(London)">O<sub>2</sub>
Arena</a>
and
announced
a
series
of
comeback
concerts
titled
<a
href="/wiki/This_Is_It_(Michael_Jackson_concerts)?qsrc=3044"
title="This
Is
It
(Michael
Jackson
concerts)">This
Is
It</a>.
The
shows
would
be
Jackson's
first
major
series
of
concerts
since
the
HIStory
World
Tour
finished
in
1997.
Jackson
suggested
possible
retirement
after
the
shows;
he
said
it
would
be
his
&quot;final
curtain
call&quot;.
The
initial
plan
was
for
10
concerts
in
London,
followed
by
shows
in
Paris,
New
York
City
and
<a
href="/wiki/Mumbai?qsrc=3044"
title="Mumbai">Mumbai</a>.
Randy
Phillips,
president
and
chief
executive
of
AEG
Live,
stated
that
the
first
10
dates
alone
would
earn
the
singer
approximately
<span
class="nowrap">&pound;50
million</span>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_grand_finale_curtain-raiser_206-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_grand_finale_curtain-raiser-206">[207]</a></sup>
The
London
residency
was
increased
to
50
dates
after
record
breaking
ticket
sales:
over
one
million
were
sold
in
less
than
two
hours.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rolling_Stone_50_dates.2C_.7B.7BNowrap.7C1_million.7D.7D_tickets_207-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rolling_Stone_50_dates.2C_.7B.7BNowrap.7C1_million.7D.7D_tickets-207">[208]</a></sup>
Jackson
rehearsed
in
Los
Angeles
in
the
weeks
leading
up
to
the
tour
under
the
direction
of
choreographer
<a
href="/wiki/Kenny_Ortega?qsrc=3044"
title="Kenny
Ortega">Kenny
Ortega</a>.
Most
of
these
rehearsals
took
place
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Staples_Center?qsrc=3044"
title="Staples
Center">Staples
Center</a>,
which
was
owned
by
AEG.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson:_The_Last_Rehearsal_208-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson:_The_Last_Rehearsal-208">[209]</a></sup>
The
concerts
would
have
commenced
on
July
13,
2009,
and
finished
on
March
6,
2010.
Less
than
three
weeks
before
the
first
show
was
due
to
begin
in
London
and
with
all
concerts
being
sold
out,
Jackson
died
after
suffering
cardiac
arrest.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_dead_at_50_after_cardiac_arrest_209-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_dead_at_50_after_cardiac_arrest-209">[210]</a></sup>
Some
time
before
his
death,
it
was
widely
stated
that
he
was
starting
a
clothing
line
with
<a
href="/wiki/Christian_Audigier?qsrc=3044"
title="Christian
Audigier">Christian
Audigier</a>;
due
to
his
death,
the
current
status
of
the
label
remains
unknown.<sup
id="cite_ref-Christian_Audigier_Michael_Jackson_Clothing_Collection_Confirmed_210-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Christian_Audigier_Michael_Jackson_Clothing_Collection_Confirmed-210">[211]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Christian_Audigier_Clothing_Line_Was_in_the_Works_211-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Christian_Audigier_Clothing_Line_Was_in_the_Works-211">[212]</a></sup></p>

style="width:182px;">

Jackson
on
stage
rehearsing
on
June
23,
2009
for
his
sold
out











<a

Is

(Michael

concert
shows

<p>Jackson's
first
posthumous
song
released
entirely
by
his
Estate
was
titled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/This_Is_It_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="This
Is
It
(Michael
Jackson
song)">This
Is
It</a>&quot;
which
Jackson
cowrote
in
the
1980s
with
<a
href="/wiki/Paul_Anka?qsrc=3044"
title="Paul
Anka">Paul
Anka</a>.
It
was
not
on
the
set
lists
for
the
concerts,
and
the
recording
was
based
on
an
old
demo
tape.
The
surviving
brothers
reunited
in
the
studio
for
the
first
time
since
1989
to
record
backing
vocals.
On
October
28,
2009,
a
documentary
film
about
the
rehearsals
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson%27s_This_Is_It?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson's
This
Is
It">Michael
Jackson's
This
Is
It</a></i>
was
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-Judge_Approves_Michael_Jackson_Film_212-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Judge_Approves_Michael_Jackson_Film-212">[213]</a></sup>
Even
though
it
ran
for
a
limited
two-week
engagement,
it
became
the
highest
grossing
documentary
or
concert
movie
of
all
time,
with
earnings
of
more
than
<span
class="nowrap">$260
million</span>
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-boxofficemojo_213-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-boxofficemojo-213">[214]</a></sup>
Jackson's
estate
received
90%
of
the
profits.<sup
id="cite_ref-Judge_OKs_Jackson_performance_film_deal_214-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Judge_OKs_Jackson_performance_film_deal-214">[215]</a></sup>
The
film
was
accompanied
by
a
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson%27s_This_Is_It_(album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson's
This
Is
It
(album)">compilation
album
of
the
same
name</a>.
Two
versions
of
the
new
song
appear
on
the
album,
which
also
featured
original
masters
of
Jackson's
hits
in
the
order
in
which
they
appear
in
the
movie,
along
with
a
bonus
disc
with
previously
unreleased
versions
of
more
Jackson
hits
as
well
as
a
spoken-word
poem
titled
&quot;Planet
Earth&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-New_Michael_Jackson_Song.2C_Album_Due_In_October_215-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-New_Michael_Jackson_Song.2C_Album_Due_In_October-215">[216]</a></sup>
At
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2009?qsrc=3044"
title="American
Music
Awards
of
2009">2009
American
Music
Awards</a>
Jackson
won
four
posthumous
awards,
two
for
him
and
two
for
his
album
<i>Number
Ones</i>,
bringing
his
total
American
Music
Awards
to
26.<sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_MJ_216-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_MJ-216">[217]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_2009_217-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_2009-217">[218]</a></sup></p>

<p>Jackson
is
survived
by
his
parents,
eight
siblings,
his
three
children,
a
host
of
nieces
and
nephews
also
with
grand
nephews
and
nieces.</p>

and

<div
class="rellink

Main
articles:









<a

of
Michael

of
Michael
Jackson</a>
and









<a
