Jackson
memorial
service">Michael
Jackson
memorial
service</a>







</div>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Michael_Jackson_Star.JPG"
class="image"><img
alt="
Image
of
Jacksons
Star
with
flowerd
and
notes
on
it"
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com:80/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Michael_Jackson_Star.JPG/180px-Michael_Jackson_Star.JPG"
width="180"
height="120"
class="thumbimage"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Michael_Jackson_Star.JPG"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="/images/wikipedia/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Fans
flocked
to
Jackson's
star
on
the
Hollywood
Walk
of
Fame,
adorning
it
with
flowers
and
notes
on
the
day
of
his
death









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>On
June
25,
2009,
Jackson
died
while
in
his
bed
at
his
rented
mansion
at
100
North
Carolwood
Drive
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Holmby_Hills,_Los_Angeles?qsrc=3044"
title="Holmby
Hills,
Los
Angeles">Holmby
Hills</a>
district
of
Los
Angeles.
Attempts
at
resuscitating
him
by
<a
href="/wiki/Conrad_Murray?qsrc=3044"
title="Conrad
Murray">Conrad
Murray</a>,
his
<a
href="/wiki/Personal_physician?qsrc=3044"
title="Personal
physician">personal
physician</a>,
were
unsuccessful.<sup
id="cite_ref-Times6580897_218-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Times6580897-218">[219]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Fire_Department?qsrc=3044"
title="Los
Angeles
Fire
Department">Los
Angeles
Fire
Department</a>
paramedics
received
a
<a
href="/wiki/9-1-1?qsrc=3044"
title="9-1-1">911</a>
call
at
12:22
(<a
href="/wiki/Pacific_Time_Zone?qsrc=3044"
title="Pacific
Time
Zone">PDT</a>,
19:22
UTC),
arriving
three
minutes
later
at
Jackson's
location.<sup
id="cite_ref-Los_Angeles_Fire_Department_recording_of_the_emergency_phone_call_made_from_Michael_Jackson.27s_home_219-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Los_Angeles_Fire_Department_recording_of_the_emergency_phone_call_made_from_Michael_Jackson.27s_home-219">[220]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Transcript_of_911_call_220-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Transcript_of_911_call-220">[221]</a></sup>
He
was
reportedly
not
breathing
and
<a
href="/wiki/Cardiopulmonary_resuscitation?qsrc=3044"
title="Cardiopulmonary
resuscitation">CPR</a>
was
performed.<sup
id="cite_ref-MSNBC_221-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MSNBC-221">[222]</a></sup>
Resuscitation
efforts
continued
en
route
to
the
<a
href="/wiki/Ronald_Reagan_UCLA_Medical_Center?qsrc=3044"
title="Ronald
Reagan
UCLA
Medical
Center">Ronald
Reagan
UCLA
Medical
Center</a>,
and
for
more
than
an
hour
after
arriving
there
at
1:13
(20:13&nbsp;UTC).
He
was
pronounced
dead
at
2:26
local
time
(21:26&nbsp;UTC).<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson.2C_King_of_Pop.2C_dies_of_cardiac_arrest_in_Los_Angeles_222-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson.2C_King_of_Pop.2C_dies_of_cardiac_arrest_in_Los_Angeles-222">[223]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-reuters_223-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-reuters-223">[224]</a></sup>
Jackson's
death
triggered
a
global
outpouring
of
grief.<sup
id="cite_ref-Times6580897_218-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Times6580897-218">[219]</a></sup></p>








<p>The
news
spread
quickly
online,
causing
websites
to
slow
down
and
<a
href="/wiki/Crash_(computing)?qsrc=3044"
title="Crash
(computing)">crash</a>
from
user
overload.
Both
<a
href="/wiki/TMZ.com?qsrc=3044"
title="TMZ.com">TMZ</a>
and
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times?qsrc=3044"
title="Los
Angeles
Times">Los
Angeles
Times</a></i>
suffered
outages.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rawlinson_224-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rawlinson-224">[225]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Google?qsrc=3044"
title="Google">Google</a>
initially
believed
that
the
input
from
millions
of
people
searching
for
&quot;Michael
Jackson&quot;
meant
that
the
search
engine
was
under
<a
href="/wiki/Distributed_denial-of-service_attack?qsrc=3044"
title="Distributed
denial-of-service
attack">DDoS
attack</a>,
and
blocked
searches
related
to
Michael
Jackson
for
30
minutes.
Twitter
reported
a
crash,
as
did
Wikipedia
at
<span
class="nowrap">3:15&nbsp;pm</span>
PDT
(22:15&nbsp;UTC).<sup
id="cite_ref-bbc21_225-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bbc21-225">[226]</a></sup>
The
<a
href="/wiki/Wikimedia_Foundation?qsrc=3044"
title="Wikimedia
Foundation">Wikimedia
Foundation</a>
reported
nearly
a
million
visitors
to
Jackson's
biography
within
one
hour,
probably
the
most
visitors
in
a
one-hour
period
to
any
article
in
Wikipedia's
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-wikipedia_226-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wikipedia-226">[227]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/AOL_Instant_Messenger?qsrc=3044"
title="AOL
Instant
Messenger">AOL
Instant
Messenger</a>
collapsed
for
40
minutes.
AOL
called
it
a
&quot;seminal
moment
in
Internet
history&quot;,
adding,
&quot;We've
never
seen
anything
like
it
in
terms
of
scope
or
depth.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-WoodJune27_227-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-WoodJune27-227">[228]</a></sup></p>








<p>Around
15%
of
Twitter
posts—or
5,000
<a
href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tweet#Noun"
title="wikt:tweet">tweets</a>
per
minute—reportedly
mentioned
Jackson
after
the
news
broke,<sup
id="cite_ref-crash_228-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-crash-228">[229]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Wortham_229-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Wortham-229">[230]</a></sup>
compared
to
the
5%
recalled
as
having
mentioned
the
<a
href="/wiki/2009_Iranian_election?qsrc=3044"
title="2009
Iranian
election">Iranian
elections</a>
or
the
<a
href="/wiki/2009_flu_pandemic?qsrc=3044"
title="2009
flu
pandemic">flu
pandemic</a>
that
had
made
headlines
earlier
in
the
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-Wortham_229-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Wortham-229">[230]</a></sup>
Overall,
<a
href="/wiki/Web_traffic?qsrc=3044"
title="Web
traffic">web
traffic</a>
ranged
from
11%
to
at
least
20%
higher
than
normal.<sup
id="cite_ref-crash_228-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-crash-228">[229]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-cnet_230-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cnet-230">[231]</a></sup>
MTV
and
<a
href="/wiki/Black_Entertainment_Television?qsrc=3044"
title="Black
Entertainment
Television">Black
Entertainment
Television</a>
(BET)
aired
<a
href="/wiki/Marathon_(television)?qsrc=3044"
title="Marathon
(television)">marathons</a>
of
Jackson's
music
videos.<sup
id="cite_ref-mtvjackson_231-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-mtvjackson-231">[232]</a></sup>
Jackson
specials
aired
on
multiple
television
stations
around
the
world.
The
British
soap
opera
<i><a
href="/wiki/EastEnders?qsrc=3044"
title="EastEnders">EastEnders</a></i>
added
a
last-minute
scene,
in
which
one
character
tells
another
about
the
news,
to
the
June
26
episode.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jacko_news_spreads_to_Eastenders_232-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jacko_news_spreads_to_Eastenders-232">[233]</a></sup>
Jackson
was
the
topic
of
every
front-page
headline
in
the
daily
British
tabloid
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Sun
(United
Kingdom)">The
Sun</a></i>
for
about
two
weeks
following
his
death.<sup
id="cite_ref-SunHeadlines_233-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-SunHeadlines-233">[234]</a></sup>
During
the
same
period,
the
three
major
U.S.
networks'
evening
newscasts—<a
href="/wiki/ABC_World_News?qsrc=3044"
title="ABC
World
News">ABC
World
News</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/CBS_Evening_News?qsrc=3044"
title="CBS
Evening
News">CBS
Evening
News</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/NBC_Nightly_News?qsrc=3044"
title="NBC
Nightly
News">NBC
Nightly
News</a>—devoted
34%
of
their
broadcast
time
to
him.<sup
id="cite_ref-newsbusters_234-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-newsbusters-234">[235]</a></sup>
Magazines
including
<i><a
href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
title="Time
(magazine)">Time</a></i>
published
commemorative
editions.<sup
id="cite_ref-people_235-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-people-235">[236]</a></sup>
A
scene
that
had
featured
Jackson's
sister
La
Toya
was
cut
from
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Br%C3%BCno?qsrc=3044"
title="Br&uuml;no">Br&uuml;no</a></i>
out
of
respect
toward
Jackson's
family.<sup
id="cite_ref-nydailynews_236-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-nydailynews-236">[237]</a></sup></p>








<p>Jackson's
memorial
was
held
on
July
7,
2009,
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Staples_Center?qsrc=3044"
title="Staples
Center">Staples
Center</a>
in
Los
Angeles,
preceded
by
a
private
family
service
at
<a
href="/wiki/Forest_Lawn_Memorial_Park_(Hollywood_Hills)?qsrc=3044#Court_of_Liberty"
title="Forest
Lawn
Memorial
Park
(Hollywood
Hills)">Forest
Lawn
Memorial
Park's
Hall
of
Liberty</a>.
Jackson's
casket
was
present
during
the
memorial
but
no
information
was
released
about
the
final
disposition
of
the
body.
The
memorial
service
was
one
of
the
most
watched
events
in
online
streaming
history.<sup
id="cite_ref-237"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-237">[238]</a></sup>
The
U.S.
audience
was
estimated
by
Nielsen
to
be
31.1
million,
an
amount
comparable
to
the
estimated
<span
class="nowrap">35.1
million</span>
that
watched
the
<a
href="/wiki/Death_and_state_funeral_of_Ronald_Reagan?qsrc=3044"
title="Death
and
state
funeral
of
Ronald
Reagan">2004
burial
of
former
president
Ronald
Reagan</a>,
and
the
estimated
<span
class="nowrap">33.1
million</span>
Americans
who
watched
the
<a
href="/wiki/Funeral_of_Diana,_Princess_of_Wales?qsrc=3044"
title="Funeral
of
Diana,
Princess
of
Wales">1997
funeral
for
Princess
Diana</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-238"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-238">[239]</a></sup></p>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey?qsrc=3044"
title="Mariah
Carey">Mariah
Carey</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Stevie_Wonder?qsrc=3044"
title="Stevie
Wonder">Stevie
Wonder</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Lionel_Richie?qsrc=3044"
title="Lionel
Richie">Lionel
Richie</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Mayer?qsrc=3044"
title="John
Mayer">John
Mayer</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Jennifer_Hudson?qsrc=3044"
title="Jennifer
Hudson">Jennifer
Hudson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
title="Usher
(entertainer)">Usher</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Jermaine_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="Jermaine
Jackson">Jermaine
Jackson</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Shaheen_Jafargholi?qsrc=3044"
title="Shaheen
Jafargholi">Shaheen
Jafargholi</a>
performed
at
the
event.
<a
href="/wiki/Berry_Gordy?qsrc=3044"
title="Berry
Gordy">Berry
Gordy</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Smokey_Robinson?qsrc=3044"
title="Smokey
Robinson">Smokey
Robinson</a>
gave
eulogies,
while
<a
href="/wiki/Queen_Latifah?qsrc=3044"
title="Queen
Latifah">Queen
Latifah</a>
read
&quot;We
had
him&quot;,
a
poem
written
for
the
occasion
by
<a
href="/wiki/Maya_Angelou?qsrc=3044"
title="Maya
Angelou">Maya
Angelou</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-telegraph_239-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-telegraph-239">[240]</a></sup>
The
Reverend
<a
href="/wiki/Al_Sharpton?qsrc=3044"
title="Al
Sharpton">Al
Sharpton</a>
received
a
standing
ovation
with
cheers
when
he
told
Jackson's
children,
&quot;Wasn't
nothing
strange
about
your
daddy.
It
was
strange
what
your
daddy
had
to
deal
with.
But
he
dealt
with
it
anyway.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-macleans_240-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-macleans-240">[241]</a></sup>
Jackson's
11-year-old
daughter,
<a
href="/wiki/Paris_Katherine_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="Paris
Katherine
Jackson">Paris
Katherine</a>,
cried
as
she
told
the
crowd,
&quot;Ever
since
I
was
born,
Daddy
has
been
the
best
father
you
could
ever
imagine&nbsp;...
I
just
wanted
to
say
I
love
him&nbsp;...
so
much.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-guardian_167-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guardian-167">[168]</a></sup>
Reverend
Lucious
Smith
provided
a
closing
prayer.<sup
id="cite_ref-radiolive_241-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-radiolive-241">[242]</a></sup>
On
August
24,
several
news
outlets
quoted
anonymous
sources
as
stating
that
the
Los
Angeles
coroner
had
decided
to
treat
Jackson's
death
as
a
homicide;
this
was
later
confirmed
by
the
coroner
on
August
28.<sup
id="cite_ref-LA_coroner_to_treat_Michael_Jackson.27s_death_as_a_homicide_242-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-LA_coroner_to_treat_Michael_Jackson.27s_death_as_a_homicide-242">[243]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_.27had_lethal_drug_levels.27_243-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_.27had_lethal_drug_levels.27-243">[244]</a></sup>
At
the
time
of
death,
Jackson
had
been
administered
<a
href="/wiki/Propofol?qsrc=3044"
title="Propofol">propofol</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Lorazepam?qsrc=3044"
title="Lorazepam">lorazepam</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Midazolam?qsrc=3044"
title="Midazolam">midazolam</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-.27WebMD.27_244-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-.27WebMD.27-244">[245]</a></sup>
Law
enforcement
officials
conducted
a
manslaughter
investigation
of
his
personal
physician,
Conrad
Murray.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Homicide_Ruling_245-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Homicide_Ruling-245">[246]</a></sup>
On
February
8,
2010,
<a
href="/wiki/People_of_the_State_of_California_v._Conrad_Robert_Murray?qsrc=3044"
title="People
of
the
State
of
California
v.
Conrad
Robert
Murray">Murray
was
charged</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/Involuntary_manslaughter?qsrc=3044"
title="Involuntary
manslaughter">involuntary
manslaughter</a>
by
prosecutors
in
Los
Angeles.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson.27s_doctor_charged_with_manslaughter_246-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson.27s_doctor_charged_with_manslaughter-246">[247]</a></sup>
Jackson
was
entombed
on
September
3,
2009,
at
<a
href="/wiki/Forest_Lawn_Memorial_Park,_Glendale?qsrc=3044"
title="Forest
Lawn
Memorial
Park,
Glendale">Forest
Lawn
Memorial
Park</a>
in
<a
href="/wiki/Glendale,_California?qsrc=3044"
title="Glendale,
California">Glendale</a>,
California.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_finally_laid_to_rest_in_Los_Angeles_247-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_finally_laid_to_rest_in_Los_Angeles-247">[248]</a></sup></p>

Tribute
of
fans
from
all
over
the
world
in
the
Forest
Lawn
Memorial
Park
on
his
first
anniversary
of
death

<p>On
June
25,
2010,
the
first
anniversary
of
Jackson's
death,
fans
traveled
to
Los
Angeles
to
pay
their
tribute
to
him.
They
visited
Jackson’s
star
on
the
Hollywood
Walk
of
Fame
and
his
family’s
home,
as
well
as
Forest
Lawn
Memorial
Park.
Many
of
the
fans
were
carrying
sunflowers
and
other
tribute
items
to
drop
off
at
the
sites.
Members
of
the
Jackson
family
and
close
friends
arrived
to
pay
their
respects.<sup
id="cite_ref-One_year_later:_Fans_gather_to_pay_tribute_to_Michael_Jackson_248-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-One_year_later:_Fans_gather_to_pay_tribute_to_Michael_Jackson-248">[249]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Familia_y_fans_de_Jackson_le_recuerdan_en_el_aniversario_de_su_muerte_249-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Familia_y_fans_de_Jackson_le_recuerdan_en_el_aniversario_de_su_muerte-249">[250]</a></sup>
Katherine
returned
to
Gary,
Indiana
to
unveil
a
granite
monument
constructed
in
the
front
yard
of
the
family
home.
The
memorial
continued
with
a
candlelight
vigil
and
a
special
performance
of
&quot;We
Are
the
World&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Gary_Indiana_Hosts_Michael_Jackson_Tribute_June_25.2C_2010_250-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Gary_Indiana_Hosts_Michael_Jackson_Tribute_June_25.2C_2010-250">[251]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Fans_honor_Michael_Jackson_in_Gary.2C_Indiana_251-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Fans_honor_Michael_Jackson_in_Gary.2C_Indiana-251">[252]</a></sup>
On
June
26,
there
was
a
protest
march
in
front
of
the
Los
Angeles
Police
Department's
Robbery-Homicide
Division
at
the
old
Parker
Center
building
and
a
petition
with
thousands
of
signatures
demanding
justice
was
delivered.<sup
id="cite_ref-A_year_after_Michael_Jackson.27s_death.2C_fan_base_remains_committed_to_keeping_memory_alive_252-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-A_year_after_Michael_Jackson.27s_death.2C_fan_base_remains_committed_to_keeping_memory_alive-252">[253]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-MJ_fans_plan_to_march_in_downtown_L.A._one_day_after_anniversary_253-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MJ_fans_plan_to_march_in_downtown_L.A._one_day_after_anniversary-253">[254]</a></sup>
The
Jackson
Family
Foundation
in
conjunction
with
Voiceplate
presented
&quot;Forever
Michael&quot;,
an
event
bringing
together
Jackson
family
members,
celebrities,
fans,
supporters
and
the
community
to
celebrate
and
honor
his
legacy.
A
portion
of
the
proceeds
were
presented
to
some
of
Jackson's
favorite
charities.
Katherine
also
introduced
her
new
book
&quot;Never
Can
Say
Goodbye&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-gimenez_254-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-gimenez-254">[255]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-michaeljackson_255-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-michaeljackson-255">[256]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Aniversario_de_muerte_de_Michael_Jackson_pasar.C3.A1_sin_grandes_homenajes_256-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Aniversario_de_muerte_de_Michael_Jackson_pasar.C3.A1_sin_grandes_homenajes-256">[257]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Death_aftermath">Death
aftermath</span></h3>








<p>After
his
death,
Jackson
became
the
best-selling
albums
artist
of
2009.
He
sold
over
8.2
million
albums
in
the
United
States,
and
a
total
of
<span
class="nowrap">35
million</span>
albums
worldwide,
in
the
12
months
that
followed
his
death.<sup
id="cite_ref-Taylor_Swift_Edges_Susan_Boyle_for_2009.27s_Top-Selling_Album_257-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Taylor_Swift_Edges_Susan_Boyle_for_2009.27s_Top-Selling_Album-257">[258]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_sells_35_million_albums_since_death_-_Entertainment_-_Access_Hollywood_-_TODAYshow.com_258-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_sells_35_million_albums_since_death_-_Entertainment_-_Access_Hollywood_-_TODAYshow.com-258">[259]</a></sup>
Jackson
became
the
first
artist
to
sell
one
million
downloads
in
a
week
in
download
history,
with
a
record-breaking
2.6
million
downloads
of
his
songs.
After
his
death
three
of
his
albums
sold
more
than
any
new
album
which
was
the
first
time
a
catalog
album
has
ever
scanned
more
sales
than
any
new
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-259"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-259">[260]</a></sup>
Jackson
also
became
the
first
artist
in
history
to
have
four
of
the
top
20
best
selling
albums
in
a
single
year
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-260"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-260">[261]</a></sup>
Following
this
surge
in
sales,
Sony
announced
that
they
had
extended
their
relationship
with
his
material.
The
distribution
rights
held
by
Sony
Music
were
due
to
expire
in
2015.<sup
id="cite_ref-wallstreet-sony_261-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wallstreet-sony-261">[262]</a></sup>
On
March
16,
2010,
Sony
Music
Entertainment,
in
a
move
spearheaded
by
its
<a
href="/wiki/Columbia/Epic_Label_Group?qsrc=3044"
title="Columbia/Epic
Label
Group">Columbia/Epic
Label
Group</a>
division,
signed
a
new
deal
with
the
Jackson
estate
to
extend
their
distribution
rights
to
his
back
catalogue
until
at
least
2017,
as
well
as
to
obtain
permission
to
release
ten
new
albums
with
previously
unreleased
material
and
new
collections
of
released
work.
On
November
4,
2010
Sony
announced
the
release
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Michael_(album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
(album)">Michael</a></i>,
the
first
posthumous
album
set
to
be
released
on
December
14,
with
the
promotional
single
released
to
the
radios
on
November
8,
titled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Breaking_News_(song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Breaking
News
(song)">Breaking
News</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-MICHAEL_Album_Announcement_262-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MICHAEL_Album_Announcement-262">[263]</a></sup>
The
deal
was
unprecedented
in
the
music
industry
as
it
is
the
most
expensive
music
contract
pertaining
to
a
single
artist
in
history;
it
reportedly
involved
Sony
Music
paying
<span
class="nowrap">$250
million</span>
for
the
deal,
with
the
Jackson
estate
getting
the
full
sum
as
well
as
its
share
of
royalties
for
all
works
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-wallstreet-sony_261-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-wallstreet-sony-261">[262]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-bbc22_263-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-bbc22-263">[264]</a></sup>
Video
game
developer
<a
href="/wiki/Ubisoft?qsrc=3044"
title="Ubisoft">Ubisoft</a>
announced
it
would
release
a
new
<a
href="/wiki/Music_game?qsrc=3044"
title="Music
game">dancing-and-singing
game</a>
featuring
Michael
Jackson
for
the
2010
holiday
season.
The
game
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson:_The_Experience?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson:
The
Experience">Michael
Jackson:
The
Experience</a></i>
will
be
among
the
first
to
use
<a
href="/wiki/Kinect?qsrc=3044"
title="Kinect">Kinect</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/PlayStation_Move?qsrc=3044"
title="PlayStation
Move">PlayStation
Move</a>,
the
respective
motion-detecting
camera
systems
for
Microsoft's
<a
href="/wiki/Xbox_360?qsrc=3044"
title="Xbox
360">Xbox
360</a>
and
Sony's
<a
href="/wiki/PlayStation_3?qsrc=3044"
title="PlayStation
3">PlayStation
3</a>
due
out
later
that
year.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Fans_Will_Moonwalk_In_Motion-Sensing_Game_264-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Fans_Will_Moonwalk_In_Motion-Sensing_Game-264">[265]</a></sup></p>








<p>Michael
Jackson
was
reported
to
be
one
of
the
largest
owners
of
<a
href="/wiki/Extraterrestrial_real_estate?qsrc=3044"
title="Extraterrestrial
real
estate">property
on
the
moon</a>.
In
2005,
he
bought
a
1,200
acre
plot
in
the
Lake
of
Dreams
and
owned
a
smaller
parcel
in
the
Sea
of
Vapours.
After
his
death,
a
crater
on
the
moon
was
renamed
Michael
Joseph
Jackson
by
The
Lunar
Republic
Society
in
Jackson's
honor.
The
crater,
officially
named
Posidonius
J,
is
located
on
an
area
of
the
moon
known
as
the
Lake
of
Dreams,
or
Lacus
Somniorum.
The
crater
is
22
kilometers
across
and
is
situated
near
Jackson's
owned
land.
A
spokesman
for
the
society
said:
&quot;The
official
designation
of
a
Lunar
crater
is
a
singular
honour
bestowed
upon
only
a
select
few
luminaries.
&quot;Among
those
receiving
this
rare
tribute
over
the
past
century
are
Leonardo
da
Vinci,
Christopher
Columbus,
Sir
Isaac
Newton,
Julius
Caesar
and
Jules
Verne.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-265"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-265">[266]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-266"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-266">[267]</a></sup></p>








<p>On
November
3,
2010,
the
theatrical
performing
company
<a
href="/wiki/Cirque_du_Soleil?qsrc=3044"
title="Cirque
du
Soleil">Cirque
du
Soleil</a>
announced
that
it
would
launch
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson:_The_Immortal_World_Tour?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson:
The
Immortal
World
Tour">Michael
Jackson:
The
Immortal
World
Tour</a>&quot;
in
October
2011
in
Montreal,
while
a
permanent
show
will
reside
in
Las
Vegas.<sup
id="cite_ref-People:_Cirque_du_Soleil_mounting_Michael_Jackson_tour_.E2.80.93_San_Jose_Mercury_News_267-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-People:_Cirque_du_Soleil_mounting_Michael_Jackson_tour_.E2.80.93_San_Jose_Mercury_News-267">[268]</a></sup>
The
90-minute
US$57M
production
will
combine
Jackson's
iconic
musical
oeuvre
and
choreography
with
the
Cirque's
signature
artistry,
dance
and
aerial
displays
involving
65
artists.<sup
id="cite_ref-www_268-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-www-268">[269]</a></sup>
The
tour
was
written
and
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Jamie_King?qsrc=3044"
title="Jamie
King">Jamie
King</a><sup
id="cite_ref-Where_to_see_Cirque_du_Soleil.27s_Michael_Jackson_tour_.E2.80.93_News_.26_Advice.2C_Travel_269-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Where_to_see_Cirque_du_Soleil.27s_Michael_Jackson_tour_.E2.80.93_News_.26_Advice.2C_Travel-269">[270]</a></sup>
and
centers
on
Jackson's
&quot;inspirational
Giving
Tree
–
the
wellspring
of
creativity
where
his
love
of
music
and
dance,
fairy
tale
and
magic,
and
the
fragile
beauty
of
nature
are
unlocked.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_.27Immortal.27_tour_opens_advance_ticket_sales_.E2.80.93_Music.2C_Arts_.26_Entertainment_270-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_.27Immortal.27_tour_opens_advance_ticket_sales_.E2.80.93_Music.2C_Arts_.26_Entertainment-270">[271]</a></sup>
On
October
3,
2011,
the
accompanying
compilation
soundtrack
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Immortal_(Michael_Jackson_album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Immortal
(Michael
Jackson
album)">Immortal</a></i>
was
announced
to
have
over
40
Jackson’s
original
recordings
re-produced
by
Kevin
Antunes.<sup
id="cite_ref-Immortal_newsletter_271-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Immortal_newsletter-271">[272]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
April
2011,
Jackson's
longtime
friend
and
billionaire
businessman
<a
href="/wiki/Mohamed_Al-Fayed?qsrc=3044"
title="Mohamed
Al-Fayed">Mohamed
Al-Fayed</a>,
chairman
of
<a
href="/wiki/Fulham_F.C.?qsrc=3044"
title="Fulham
F.C.">Fulham
F.C.</a>,
unveiled
a
statue
of
Jackson
outside
the
club's
stadium,
<a
href="/wiki/Craven_Cottage?qsrc=3044"
title="Craven
Cottage">Craven
Cottage</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-English_Premier_League:_Fans_can_.27go_to_hell.27.2C_says_Fulham_owner_Mohamed_Al_Fayed_272-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-English_Premier_League:_Fans_can_.27go_to_hell.27.2C_says_Fulham_owner_Mohamed_Al_Fayed-272">[273]</a></sup>
Fulham
fans
were
however
bemused
by
the
statue
and
failed
to
understand
the
relevance
of
Jackson
to
the
club.<sup
id="cite_ref-Fulham_fans_cry_foul_over_.27bizarre.27_Michael_Jackson_statue_273-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Fulham_fans_cry_foul_over_.27bizarre.27_Michael_Jackson_statue-273">[274]</a></sup>
Al
Fayed
however
defended
the
statue
and
told
the
fans
to
'go
to
hell'
if
they
didn't
appreciate
the
statue.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Fulham_FC_statue_defended_by_Al_Fayed_274-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Fulham_FC_statue_defended_by_Al_Fayed-274">[275]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
2012,
in
an
attempt
to
end
family
public
feuding,
Jackson's
brother
<a
href="/wiki/Jermaine_Jackson?qsrc=3044"
title="Jermaine
Jackson">Jermaine
Jackson</a>
retracted
his
signature
on
a
letter
made
public
criticizing
executors
of
Michael
Jackson's
estate
and
his
mother's
advisers
concerning
the
legitimacy
of
his
brothers
will.<sup
id="cite_ref-275"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-275">[276]</a></sup>
T.J.
Jackson,
son
of
Tito
Jackson,
was
given
co-guardianship
of
Michael's
kids
after
false
reports
surfaced
of
Katherine
Jackson
going
missing.<sup
id="cite_ref-276"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-276">[277]</a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Artistry">Artistry</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Influences">Influences</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:142px;">









<a

silver
colored
statue
of
a
male.

statue

and

legs
spaced
apart.
The

have
wrinkles
and
it
is

<div

<a

</div>
One
of
many
identical
statues,
positioned
throughout
Europe
to
promote











<i>HIStory</i>









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Jackson's
music
took
root
in
<a
href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues?qsrc=3044"
title="Rhythm
and
blues">R&amp;B</a>,
pop
and
<a
href="/wiki/Soul_music?qsrc=3044"
title="Soul
music">soul</a>.
He
had
been
influenced
by
the
work
of
contemporary
musicians
such
as
<a
href="/wiki/Little_Richard?qsrc=3044"
title="Little
Richard">Little
Richard</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/James_Brown?qsrc=3044"
title="James
Brown">James
Brown</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Jackie_Wilson?qsrc=3044"
title="Jackie
Wilson">Jackie
Wilson</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Diana_Ross?qsrc=3044"
title="Diana
Ross">Diana
Ross</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Fred_Astaire?qsrc=3044"
title="Fred
Astaire">Fred
Astaire</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Sammy_Davis,_Jr.?qsrc=3044"
title="Sammy
Davis,
Jr.">Sammy
Davis,
Jr.</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Gene_Kelly?qsrc=3044"
title="Gene
Kelly">Gene
Kelly</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-slateinfo_277-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-slateinfo-277">[278]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/David_Ruffin?qsrc=3044"
title="David
Ruffin">David
Ruffin</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-rollingstonedavid_278-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rollingstonedavid-278">[279]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/The_Isley_Brothers?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Isley
Brothers">The
Isley
Brothers</a>,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bee_Gees?qsrc=3044"
title="Bee
Gees">Bee
Gees</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/West_Side_Story?qsrc=3044"
title="West
Side
Story">West
Side
Story</a>
dancers,
to
whom
he
made
a
tribute
in
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Beat_It?qsrc=3044"
title="Beat
It">Beat
It</a>&quot;
and
in
the
&quot;Bad&quot;
video.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jones2005_279-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jones2005-279">[280]</a></sup>
According
to
<a
href="/wiki/David_Winters_(choreographer)?qsrc=3044"
title="David
Winters
(choreographer)">David
Winters</a>,
who
met
and
befriended
Jackson
while
choreographing
the
1971
<a
href="/wiki/Diana_Ross?qsrc=3044"
title="Diana
Ross">Diana
Ross</a>
TV
Special
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Diana!?qsrc=3044"
title="Diana!">Diana!</a>&quot;,
(which
was
also
Jackson's
first
solo
debut
outside
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Jackson_5?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Jackson
5">The
Jackson
5</a>),
Jackson
watched
<a
href="/wiki/West_Side_Story?qsrc=3044"
title="West
Side
Story">West
Side
Story</a>
almost
every
week
and
it
was
his
favorite
film.<sup
id="cite_ref-Magickpapers.com_280-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Magickpapers.com-280">[281]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Thank_you_BigBearJohn:_here.27s_also_David_Winters_281-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Thank_you_BigBearJohn:_here.27s_also_David_Winters-281">[282]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Remembering_Michael_Jackson.2C_On_Screen_282-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Remembering_Michael_Jackson.2C_On_Screen-282">[283]</a></sup>
While
Little
Richard
had
a
substantial
influence
on
Jackson,<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_saved_my_life_283-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_saved_my_life-283">[284]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-imdb_284-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-imdb-284">[285]</a></sup>
James
Brown
was
Jackson's
greatest
inspiration.
In
reference
to
Brown,
Jackson
declared:
&quot;Ever
since
I
was
a
small
child,
no
more
than
like
six
years
old,
my
mother
would
wake
me
no
matter
what
time
it
was,
if
I
was
sleeping,
no
matter
what
I
was
doing,
to
watch
the
television
to
see
the
master
at
work.
And
when
I
saw
him
move,
I
was
mesmerized.
I
had
never
seen
a
performer
perform
like
James
Brown,
and
right
then
and
there
I
knew
that
was
exactly
what
I
wanted
to
do
for
the
rest
of
my
life
because
of
James
Brown.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-James_Brown.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Jackson_Attends_Brown.27s_Public_Funeral.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Contactmusic_News_285-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-James_Brown.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Jackson_Attends_Brown.27s_Public_Funeral.C2.A0.E2.80.93_Contactmusic_News-285">[286]</a></sup></p>








<p>The
young
Michael
Jackson
owed
his
vocal
technique
in
large
part
to
Diana
Ross.
Not
only
a
mother
figure
to
him,
she
was
often
observed
in
rehearsal
as
an
accomplished
performer.
He
later
expressed:
&quot;I
got
to
know
her
well.
She
taught
me
so
much.
I
used
to
just
sit
in
the
corner
and
watch
the
way
she
moved.
She
was
art
in
motion.
I
studied
the
way
she
moved,
the
way
she
sang&nbsp;–
just
the
way
she
was.&quot;
He
told
her:
&quot;I
want
to
be
just
like
you,
Diana.&quot;
She
said:
&quot;You
just
be
yourself.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli23_286-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli23-286">[287]</a></sup>
But
Jackson
owed
part
of
his
enduring
style—especially
his
use
of
the
<i>oooh</i>
interjection—to
Ross.
From
a
young
age,
Jackson
often
punctuated
his
verses
with
a
sudden
exclamation
of
<i>oooh</i>.
Diana
Ross
had
used
this
effect
on
many
of
the
songs
recorded
with
<a
href="/wiki/The_Supremes?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Supremes">The
Supremes</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli24_287-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli24-287">[288]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_themes_and_genres">Musical
themes
and
genres</span></h3>








<p>Unlike
many
artists,
Jackson
did
not
write
his
songs
on
paper.
Instead
he
would
dictate
into
a
sound
recorder,
and
when
recording
he
would
sing
the
lyrics
from
memory.<sup
id="cite_ref-taraborrelli25_288-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-taraborrelli25-288">[289]</a></sup>
In
most
of
his
songs,
such
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Billie_Jean?qsrc=3044"
title="Billie
Jean">Billie
Jean</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Who_Is_It_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Who
Is
It
(Michael
Jackson
song)">Who
Is
It</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Tabloid_Junkie?qsrc=3044"
title="Tabloid
Junkie">Tabloid
Junkie</a>&quot;,
he
would
beatbox
and
imitate
the
instruments
using
his
voice
instead
of
playing
the
actual
instruments,
along
with
other
sounds.
Jackson
noted
that
it
is
easier
to
sing
a
drum
line,
or
sing
a
bass,
instead
of
playing
a
drum
line
or
a
bass
with
an
instrument.
Several
critics
have
said
that
Jackson's
distinct
voice
was
able
to
replace
any
instrument
convincingly.
Steve
Huey
of
<a
href="/wiki/Allmusic?qsrc=3044"
title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a>
said
that,
throughout
his
solo
career,
Jackson's
versatility
allowed
him
to
experiment
with
various
themes
and
genres.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
As
a
musician,
he
ranged
from
Motown's
dance
fare
and
ballads
to
<a
href="/wiki/Techno?qsrc=3044"
title="Techno">techno</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/House_music?qsrc=3044"
title="House
music">house</a>-edged
<a
href="/wiki/New_jack_swing?qsrc=3044"
title="New
jack
swing">new
jack
swing</a>
to
work
that
incorporates
both
<a
href="/wiki/Funk?qsrc=3044"
title="Funk">funk</a>
rhythms
and
<a
href="/wiki/Hard_rock?qsrc=3044"
title="Hard
rock">hard
rock</a>
guitar.<sup
id="cite_ref-rollingstone_98-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rollingstone-98">[99]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Help_290-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Help-290">[291]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_Thriller_291-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG_Thriller-291">[292]</a></sup></p>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:182px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg"
class="image"><img
alt="A
black
and
white
photo
of
a
male
holding
a
microphone
singing"
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com:80/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg/180px-Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg"
width="180"
height="137"
class="thumbimage"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="/images/wikipedia/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Jackson
in
1988,
performing
live
at
his
record-breaking
Bad
world
tour









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>According
to
Huey,
<i>Thriller</i>
refined
the
strengths
of
<i>Off
the
Wall</i>;
the
dance
and
rock
tracks
were
more
aggressive,
while
the
pop
tunes
and
ballads
were
softer
and
more
soulful.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
Notable
tracks
included
the
ballads
&quot;The
Lady
in
My
Life&quot;,
&quot;Human
Nature&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Girl_Is_Mine?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Girl
Is
Mine">The
Girl
Is
Mine</a>&quot;;
the
funk
pieces
&quot;Billie
Jean&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wanna_Be_Startin%27_Somethin%27?qsrc=3044"
title="Wanna
Be
Startin'
Somethin'">Wanna
Be
Startin'
Somethin'</a>&quot;;
and
the
post-disco
set
&quot;Baby
Be
Mine&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/P.Y.T._(Pretty_Young_Thing)?qsrc=3044"
title="P.Y.T.
(Pretty
Young
Thing)">P.Y.T.
(Pretty
Young
Thing)</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Help_290-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Help-290">[291]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_Thriller_291-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG_Thriller-291">[292]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Slant_Thriller_292-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Slant_Thriller-292">[293]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-RS_Thriller_293-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_Thriller-293">[294]</a></sup>
With
<i>Thriller</i>,
Christopher
Connelly
of
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
commented
that
Jackson
developed
his
long
association
with
the
subliminal
theme
of
<a
href="/wiki/Paranoia?qsrc=3044"
title="Paranoia">paranoia</a>
and
darker
imagery.<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_Thriller_293-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_Thriller-293">[294]</a></sup>
Allmusic's
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine?qsrc=3044"
title="Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine">Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine</a>
noted
this
is
evident
on
the
songs
&quot;Billie
Jean&quot;
and
&quot;Wanna
Be
Startin'
Somethin'&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_Thriller_291-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG_Thriller-291">[292]</a></sup>
In
&quot;Billie
Jean&quot;,
Jackson
sings
about
an
obsessive
fan
who
alleges
he
has
fathered
a
child
of
hers.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
In
&quot;Wanna
Be
Startin'
Somethin'&quot;
he
argues
against
gossip
and
the
media.<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_Thriller_293-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_Thriller-293">[294]</a></sup>
&quot;Beat
It&quot;
decried
gang
violence
in
an
homage
to
<i><a
href="/wiki/West_Side_Story?qsrc=3044"
title="West
Side
Story">West
Side
Story</a></i>,
and
was
Jackson's
first
successful
rock
cross-over
piece,
according
to
Huey.<sup
id="cite_ref-rollingstone_98-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rollingstone-98">[99]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
He
also
observed
that
the
title
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Thriller_(song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Thriller
(song)">Thriller</a>&quot;
began
Jackson's
interest
with
the
theme
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Supernatural?qsrc=3044"
title="Supernatural">supernatural</a>,
a
topic
he
revisited
in
subsequent
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
In
1985,
Jackson
co-wrote
the
charity
anthem
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/We_Are_the_World?qsrc=3044"
title="We
Are
the
World">We
Are
the
World</a>&quot;;
humanitarian
themes
later
became
a
recurring
theme
in
his
lyrics
and
public
persona.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup></p>

<p>In
<i>Bad</i>,
Jackson's
concept
of
the
predatory
lover
can
be
seen
on
the
rock
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Dirty_Diana?qsrc=3044"
title="Dirty
Diana">Dirty
Diana</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Bad_298-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Bad-298">[299]</a></sup>
The
lead
single
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Just_Can%27t_Stop_Loving_You?qsrc=3044"
title="I
Just
Can't
Stop
Loving
You">I
Just
Can't
Stop
Loving
You</a>&quot;
is
a
traditional
love
ballad,
while
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Man_in_the_Mirror?qsrc=3044"
title="Man
in
the
Mirror">Man
in
the
Mirror</a>&quot;
is
an
anthemic
ballad
of
confession
and
resolution.<sup
id="cite_ref-TIME2_78-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TIME2-78">[79]</a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Smooth_Criminal?qsrc=3044"
title="Smooth
Criminal">Smooth
Criminal</a>&quot;
was
an
evocation
of
bloody
assault,
rape
and
likely
murder.<sup
id="cite_ref-TIME2_78-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TIME2-78">[79]</a></sup>
Allmusic's
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_Thomas_Erlewine?qsrc=3044"
title="Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine">Stephen
Thomas
Erlewine</a>
states
that
<i>Dangerous</i>
presents
Jackson
as
a
very
paradoxical
individual.<sup
id="cite_ref-ALG_Dangerous_299-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALG_Dangerous-299">[300]</a></sup>
He
comments
the
album
is
more
diverse
than
his
previous
<i>Bad</i>,
as
it
appeals
to
an
urban
audience
while
also
attracting
the
middle
class
with
anthems
like
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Heal_the_World?qsrc=3044"
title="Heal
the
World">Heal
the
World</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-ALG_Dangerous_299-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALG_Dangerous-299">[300]</a></sup>
The
first
half
of
the
record
is
dedicated
to
new
jack
swing,
including
songs
like
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Jam_(song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Jam
(song)">Jam</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Remember_the_Time?qsrc=3044"
title="Remember
the
Time">Remember
the
Time</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Dangerous_300-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Dangerous-300">[301]</a></sup>
The
album
is
Jackson's
first
where
social
ills
become
a
primary
theme;
&quot;Why
You
Wanna
Trip
on
Me&quot;,
for
example,
protests
against
world
hunger,
AIDS,
homelessness
and
drugs.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Dangerous_300-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Dangerous-300">[301]</a></sup>
<i>Dangerous</i>
contains
sexually
charged
efforts
such
as
the
multifaceted
love
song,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_the_Closet?qsrc=3044"
title="In
the
Closet">In
the
Closet</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Dangerous_300-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Dangerous-300">[301]</a></sup>
The
title
track
continues
the
theme
of
the
predatory
lover
and
compulsive
desire.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Dangerous_300-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Dangerous-300">[301]</a></sup>
The
second
half
includes
introspective,
pop-gospel
anthems
such
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Will_You_Be_There?qsrc=3044"
title="Will
You
Be
There">Will
You
Be
There</a>&quot;,
&quot;Heal
the
World&quot;
and
&quot;Keep
the
Faith&quot;;
these
songs
show
Jackson
opening
up
about
various
personal
struggles
and
worries.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Dangerous_300-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Dangerous-300">[301]</a></sup>
In
the
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Gone_Too_Soon?qsrc=3044"
title="Gone
Too
Soon">Gone
Too
Soon</a>&quot;,
Jackson
gives
tribute
to
his
friend
<a
href="/wiki/Ryan_White?qsrc=3044"
title="Ryan
White">Ryan
White</a>
and
the
plight
of
those
with
AIDS.<sup
id="cite_ref-TWP_Dangerous_301-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TWP_Dangerous-301">[302]</a></sup></p>








<p><i>HIStory</i>
creates
an
atmosphere
of
paranoia.<sup
id="cite_ref-ALG_HIStory_302-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALG_HIStory-302">[303]</a></sup>
Its
content
focuses
on
the
hardships
and
public
struggles
Jackson
went
through
just
prior
to
its
production.
In
the
new
jack
swing-funk-rock
efforts
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Scream/Childhood?qsrc=3044"
title="Scream/Childhood">Scream</a>&quot;
and
&quot;Tabloid
Junkie&quot;,
along
with
the
R&amp;B
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/You_Are_Not_Alone?qsrc=3044"
title="You
Are
Not
Alone">You
Are
Not
Alone</a>&quot;,
Jackson
retaliates
against
the
injustice
and
isolation
he
feels,
and
directs
much
of
his
anger
at
the
media.<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_HIStory_303-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_HIStory-303">[304]</a></sup>
In
the
introspective
ballad
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Stranger_in_Moscow?qsrc=3044"
title="Stranger
in
Moscow">Stranger
in
Moscow</a>&quot;,
Jackson
laments
over
his
&quot;fall
from
grace&quot;,
while
songs
like
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Earth_Song?qsrc=3044"
title="Earth
Song">Earth
Song</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Scream/Childhood?qsrc=3044"
title="Scream/Childhood">Childhood</a>&quot;,
&quot;Little
Susie&quot;
and
&quot;Smile&quot;
are
all
operatic
pop
pieces.<sup
id="cite_ref-ALG_HIStory_302-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALG_HIStory-302">[303]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-RS_HIStory_303-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_HIStory-303">[304]</a></sup>
In
the
track
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/D.S._(song)?qsrc=3044"
title="D.S.
(song)">D.S.</a>&quot;,
Jackson
launched
a
verbal
attack
against
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Sneddon?qsrc=3044"
title="Tom
Sneddon">Tom
Sneddon</a>.
He
describes
Sneddon
as
an
antisocial,
white
supremacist
who
wanted
to
&quot;get
my
ass,
dead
or
alive&quot;.
Of
the
song,
Sneddon
said,
&quot;I
have
not—shall
we
say—done
him
the
honor
of
listening
to
it,
but
I've
been
told
that
it
ends
with
the
sound
of
a
gunshot&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Sneddon_profile_304-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Sneddon_profile-304">[305]</a></sup>
<i>Invincible</i>
found
Jackson
working
heavily
with
producer
Rodney
Jerkins.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
It
is
a
record
made
up
of
urban
soul
like
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Cry_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Cry
(Michael
Jackson
song)">Cry</a>&quot;
and
&quot;The
Lost
Children&quot;,
ballads
such
as
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Speechless_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Speechless
(Michael
Jackson
song)">Speechless</a>&quot;,
&quot;Break
of
Dawn&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Butterflies_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Butterflies
(Michael
Jackson
song)">Butterflies</a>&quot;
and
mixes
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music?qsrc=3044"
title="Hip
hop
music">hip-hop</a>,
pop
and
<a
href="/wiki/R%26B?qsrc=3044"
title="R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>
in
&quot;2000
Watts&quot;,
&quot;Heartbreaker&quot;
and
&quot;Invincible&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-ALG_Invincible_305-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ALG_Invincible-305">[306]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-NME_Invincible_306-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NME_Invincible-306">[307]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Vocal_style">Vocal
style</span></h3>








<p>Jackson
sang
from
childhood,
and
over
time
his
voice
and
vocal
style
changed
noticeably.
Between
1971
and
1975,
Jackson's
voice
descended
from
boy
soprano
to
high
tenor.<sup
id="cite_ref-brac_414_307-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brac_414-307">[308]</a></sup>
His
vocal
range
as
an
adult
was
F2-E♭6.
Jackson
first
used
a
technique
called
the
&quot;vocal
hiccup&quot;
in
1973,
starting
with
the
song
&quot;It's
Too
Late
to
Change
the
Time&quot;
from
<a
href="/wiki/The_Jackson_5?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Jackson
5">The
Jackson
5</a>'s
<i><a
href="/wiki/G.I.T.:_Get_It_Together?qsrc=3044"
title="G.I.T.:
Get
It
Together">G.I.T.:
Get
It
Together</a></i>
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-brown_308-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-brown-308">[309]</a></sup>
Jackson
did
not
use
the
hiccup
technique—
somewhat
like
a
gulping
for
air
or
gasping—
fully
until
the
recording
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Off_the_Wall_(album)?qsrc=3044"
title="Off
the
Wall
(album)">Off
the
Wall</a></i>:
it
can
be
seen
in
full
force
in
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Shake_Your_Body_(Down_to_the_Ground)?qsrc=3044"
title="Shake
Your
Body
(Down
to
the
Ground)">Shake
Your
Body
(Down
to
the
Ground)</a>&quot;
promotional
video.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_22_19-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_22-19">[20]</a></sup>
With
the
arrival
of
<i>Off
the
Wall</i>
in
the
late
1970s,
Jackson's
abilities
as
a
vocalist
were
well
regarded.
At
the
time,
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
compared
his
vocals
to
the
&quot;breathless,
dreamy
stutter&quot;
of
Stevie
Wonder.
Their
analysis
was
also
that
&quot;Jackson's
feathery-timbred
tenor
is
extraordinarily
beautiful.
It
slides
smoothly
into
a
startling
<a
href="/wiki/Falsetto?qsrc=3044"
title="Falsetto">falsetto</a>
that's
used
very
daringly&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-AMG_OTW_309-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMG_OTW-309">[310]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-RS_OTW_310-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_OTW-310">[311]</a></sup>
1982
saw
the
release
of
<i>Thriller</i>,
and
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
was
of
the
opinion
that
Jackson
was
then
singing
in
a
&quot;fully
adult
voice&quot;
that
was
&quot;tinged
by
sadness&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_Thriller_293-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_Thriller-293">[294]</a></sup></p>








<p>A
distinctive
deliberate
mispronunciation
of
&quot;come
on&quot;,
used
frequently
by
Jackson,
occasionally
spelled
&quot;cha'mone&quot;
or
&quot;shamone&quot;,
is
also
a
staple
in
impressions
and
caricatures
of
him.<sup
id="cite_ref-Pink_Grease_311-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Pink_Grease-311">[312]</a></sup>
The
turn
of
the
1990s
saw
the
release
of
the
introspective
album
<i>Dangerous</i>.
<i>The
New
York
Times</i>
noted
that
on
some
tracks,
&quot;he
gulps
for
breath,
his
voice
quivers
with
anxiety
or
drops
to
a
desperate
whisper,
hissing
through
clenched
teeth&quot;
and
he
had
a
&quot;wretched
tone&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Dangerous_300-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Dangerous-300">[301]</a></sup>
When
singing
of
brotherhood
or
self-esteem
the
musician
would
return
to
&quot;smooth&quot;
vocals.<sup
id="cite_ref-NYT_Dangerous_300-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-NYT_Dangerous-300">[301]</a></sup>
When
commenting
on
<i>Invincible</i>,
<i>Rolling
Stone</i>
were
of
the
opinion
that—at
the
age
of
43—Jackson
still
performed
&quot;exquisitely
voiced
rhythm
tracks
and
vibrating
vocal
harmonies&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-RS_Invincible_312-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-RS_Invincible-312">[313]</a></sup>
Nelson
George
summed
up
Jackson's
vocals
by
stating
&quot;The
grace,
the
aggression,
the
growling,
the
natural
boyishness,
the
falsetto,
the
smoothness—that
combination
of
elements
mark
him
as
a
major
vocalist&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_24_294-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_24-294">[295]</a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Music_videos_and_choreography">Music
videos
and
choreography</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:142px;">

single
whited

glave"

<div

</div>
The
iconic
crystal
rhinestone
studded
glove
worn
by
Jackson
when
performing
the
moonwalk
on
Motown
25









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Jackson
has
also
been
referred
to
as
the
King
of
Music
Videos,<sup
id="cite_ref-collecters_313-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-collecters-313">[314]</a></sup>
Steve
Huey
of
Allmusic
observed
how
Jackson
transformed
the
music
video
into
an
art
form
and
a
promotional
tool
through
complex
story
lines,
dance
routines,
special
effects
and
famous
cameo
appearances;
simultaneously
breaking
down
racial
barriers.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-8"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
Before
<i>Thriller</i>,
Jackson
struggled
to
receive
coverage
on
MTV,
allegedly
because
he
was
African
American.<sup
id="cite_ref-blender_314-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-blender-314">[315]</a></sup>
Pressure
from
CBS
Records
persuaded
MTV
to
start
showing
&quot;Billie
Jean&quot;
and
later
&quot;Beat
It&quot;,
leading
to
a
lengthy
partnership
with
Jackson,
also
helping
other
black
music
artists
gain
recognition.<sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_changes_the_rules_of_the_music_video_315-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_changes_the_rules_of_the_music_video-315">[316]</a></sup>
MTV
employees
deny
any
racism
in
their
coverage,
or
pressure
to
change
their
stance.
MTV
maintains
that
they
played
rock
music,
regardless
of
race.<sup
id="cite_ref-findarticles_316-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-findarticles-316">[317]</a></sup>
The
popularity
of
his
videos
on
MTV
helped
to
put
the
relatively
young
channel
&quot;on
the
map&quot;;
MTV's
focus
shifted
in
favor
of
pop
and
R&amp;B.<sup
id="cite_ref-ABCNews_317-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ABCNews-317">[318]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Jackson_changes_the_rules_of_the_music_video_315-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Jackson_changes_the_rules_of_the_music_video-315">[316]</a></sup>
His
performance
on
<i>Motown
25:
Yesterday,
Today,
Forever</i>
changed
the
scope
of
live
stage
show;
&quot;That
Jackson
lip-synced
'Billie
Jean'
is,
in
itself,
not
extraordinary,
but
the
fact
that
it
did
not
change
the
impact
of
the
performance
is
extraordinary;
whether
the
performance
was
live
or
lip-synced
made
no
difference
to
the
audience&quot;
thus
creating
an
era
in
which
artists
re-create
the
spectacle
of
music
video
imagery
on
stage.<sup
id="cite_ref-MT25_318-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MT25-318">[319]</a></sup>
Short
films
like
<i><a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson%27s_Thriller?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson's
Thriller">Thriller</a></i>
largely
remained
unique
to
Jackson,
while
the
group
dance
sequence
in
&quot;Beat
It&quot;
has
frequently
been
imitated.<sup
id="cite_ref-The_Thriller_Special_Edition_Audio_319-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-The_Thriller_Special_Edition_Audio-319">[320]</a></sup>
The
choreography
in
<i>Thriller</i>
has
become
a
part
of
global
pop
culture,
replicated
everywhere
from
<a
href="/wiki/Cinema_of_India?qsrc=3044"
title="Cinema
of
India">Indian
films</a>
to
<a
href="/wiki/Thriller_(viral_video)?qsrc=3044"
title="Thriller
(viral
video)">prisons
in
the
Philippines</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Philippine_jailhouse_rocks_to_Thriller_320-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Philippine_jailhouse_rocks_to_Thriller-320">[321]</a></sup>
The
<i>Thriller</i>
short
film
marked
an
increase
in
scale
for
music
videos,
and
has
been
named
the
most
successful
music
video
ever
by
the
<i>Guinness
World
Records</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-World_Records_100-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-World_Records-100">[101]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
19-minute
music
video
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Bad_(Michael_Jackson_song)?qsrc=3044"
title="Bad
(Michael
Jackson
song)">Bad</a>&quot;—directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese?qsrc=3044"
title="Martin
Scorsese">Martin
Scorsese</a>—Jackson
began
using
sexual
imagery
and
choreography
not
previously
seen
in
his
work.
He
occasionally
grabbed
or
touched
his
chest,
torso
and
crotch.
When
asked
by
Oprah
in
the
1993
interview
about
why
he
grabbed
his
crotch,
he
replied,
&quot;I
think
it
happens
subliminally&quot;
and
he
described
it
as
something
that
was
not
planned,
but
rather,
as
something
that
was
compelled
by
the
music.
&quot;Bad&quot;
garnered
a
mixed
reception
from
both
fans
and
critics;
<i>Time</i>
magazine
described
it
as
&quot;infamous&quot;.
The
video
also
featured
<a
href="/wiki/Wesley_Snipes?qsrc=3044"
title="Wesley
Snipes">Wesley
Snipes</a>;
in
the
future
Jackson's
videos
would
often
feature
famous
cameo
roles.<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_370.E2.80.93373_71-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_370.E2.80.93373-71">[72]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Who.27s_Bad.3F_TIME_321-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Who.27s_Bad.3F_TIME-321">[322]</a></sup>
For
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Smooth_Criminal?qsrc=3044"
title="Smooth
Criminal">Smooth
Criminal</a>&quot;,
Jackson
experimented
with
an
innovative
&quot;anti-gravity
lean&quot;
in
his
performances.
The
maneuver
required
special
shoes
for
which
he
was
granted
U.S.
Patent
No.
5,255,452.<sup
id="cite_ref-tompkins_322-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tompkins-322">[323]</a></sup>
Although
the
music
video
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Leave_Me_Alone?qsrc=3044"
title="Leave
Me
Alone">Leave
Me
Alone</a>&quot;
was
not
officially
released
in
the
US,
in
1989,
it
was
nominated
for
three
<i>Billboard</i>
Music
Video
Awards;<sup
id="cite_ref-323"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-323">[324]</a></sup>
the
same
year
it
won
a
Golden
Lion
Award
for
the
quality
of
the
special
effects
used
in
its
production.
In
1990,
&quot;Leave
Me
Alone&quot;
won
a
Grammy
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Short_Form_Music_Video?qsrc=3044"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Short
Form
Music
Video">Best
Music
Video,
Short
Form</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_43-44_97-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_43-44-97">[98]</a></sup></p>








<p>He
received
the
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Vanguard_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="MTV
Video
Vanguard
Award">MTV
Video
Vanguard
Award</a>
in
1988
and
the
MTV
Video
Vanguard
Artist
of
the
Decade
Award
in
1990
to
celebrate
his
accomplishments
in
the
art
form
in
the
1980s;
in
1991
the
first
award
was
renamed
in
his
honor.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_45-46_115-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_45-46-115">[116]</a></sup>
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Black_or_White?qsrc=3044"
title="Black
or
White">Black
or
White</a>&quot;
was
accompanied
by
a
controversial
music
video,
which,
on
November
14,
1991,
simultaneously
premiered
in
27
countries
with
an
estimated
audience
of
500&nbsp;million
people,
the
largest
viewing
ever
for
a
music
video.<sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_achievements_114-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_achievements-114">[115]</a></sup>
It
featured
scenes
construed
as
having
a
sexual
nature
as
well
as
depictions
of
violence.
The
offending
scenes
in
the
final
half
of
the
14-minute
version
were
edited
out
to
prevent
the
video
from
being
banned,
and
Jackson
apologized.<sup
id="cite_ref-.27.27Dangerous.27.27_on_Film_324-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-.27.27Dangerous.27.27_on_Film-324">[325]</a></sup>
Along
with
Jackson,
it
featured
<a
href="/wiki/Macaulay_Culkin?qsrc=3044"
title="Macaulay
Culkin">Macaulay
Culkin</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Peggy_Lipton?qsrc=3044"
title="Peggy
Lipton">Peggy
Lipton</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/George_Wendt?qsrc=3044"
title="George
Wendt">George
Wendt</a>.
It
helped
usher
in
<a
href="/wiki/Morphing?qsrc=3044"
title="Morphing">morphing</a>
as
an
important
technology
in
music
videos.<sup
id="cite_ref-campbell26_325-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-campbell26-325">[326]</a></sup></p>








<p>&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Remember_the_Time?qsrc=3044"
title="Remember
the
Time">Remember
the
Time</a>&quot;
was
an
elaborate
production,
and
became
one
of
his
longest
videos
at
over
nine
minutes.
Set
in
<a
href="/wiki/Ancient_Egypt?qsrc=3044"
title="Ancient
Egypt">ancient
Egypt</a>,
it
featured
groundbreaking
<a
href="/wiki/Visual_effects?qsrc=3044"
title="Visual
effects">visual
effects</a>
and
appearances
by
<a
href="/wiki/Eddie_Murphy?qsrc=3044"
title="Eddie
Murphy">Eddie
Murphy</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Iman_(model)?qsrc=3044"
title="Iman
(model)">Iman</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Magic_Johnson?qsrc=3044"
title="Magic
Johnson">Magic
Johnson</a>,
along
with
a
distinct
complex
dance
routine.<sup
id="cite_ref-campbell27_326-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-campbell27-326">[327]</a></sup>
The
video
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/In_the_Closet?qsrc=3044"
title="In
the
Closet">In
the
Closet</a>&quot;
was
Jackson's
most
sexually
provocative
piece.
It
featured
supermodel
<a
href="/wiki/Naomi_Campbell?qsrc=3044"
title="Naomi
Campbell">Naomi
Campbell</a>
in
a
courtship
dance
with
Jackson.
The
video
was
banned
in
South
Africa
because
of
its
imagery.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_45-46_115-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_45-46-115">[116]</a></sup></p>








<p>The
music
video
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Scream/Childhood?qsrc=3044"
title="Scream/Childhood">Scream</a>&quot;,
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Mark_Romanek?qsrc=3044"
title="Mark
Romanek">Mark
Romanek</a>
and
production
designer
Tom
Foden,
is
one
of
Jackson's
most
critically
acclaimed.
In
1995,
it
gained
11
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards">MTV
Video
Music
Award
Nominations</a>—more
than
any
other
music
video—and
won
&quot;Best
Dance
Video&quot;,
&quot;Best
Choreography&quot;,
and
&quot;Best
Art
Direction&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-TCI_327-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TCI-327">[328]</a></sup>
The
song
and
its
accompanying
video
are
a
response
to
the
backlash
Jackson
received
from
the
media
after
being
accused
of
child
molestation
in
1993.<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Interview_Raises_Questions.2C_Answers_328-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Interview_Raises_Questions.2C_Answers-328">[329]</a></sup>
A
year
later,
it
won
a
Grammy
for
Best
Music
Video,
Short
Form;
shortly
afterwards
<i>Guinness
World
Records</i>
listed
it
as
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_most_expensive_music_videos?qsrc=3044"
title="List
of
most
expensive
music
videos">most
expensive
music
video
ever
made</a>
at
a
cost
of
$7&nbsp;million.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Guinness_World_Records_2006_329-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Guinness_World_Records_2006-329">[330]</a></sup></p>








<p>&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Earth_Song?qsrc=3044"
title="Earth
Song">Earth
Song</a>&quot;
was
accompanied
by
an
expensive
and
well-received
music
video
that
gained
a
Grammy
nomination
for
Best
Music
Video,
Short
Form
in
1997.
The
video
had
an
environmental
theme,
showing
images
of
animal
cruelty,
deforestation,
pollution
and
war.
Using
special
effects,
time
is
reversed
so
that
life
returns,
wars
end,
and
the
forests
re-grow.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-.27.27HIStory.27.27_on_Film_volume_II_330-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-.27.27HIStory.27.27_on_Film_volume_II-330">[331]</a></sup>
Released
in
1997
and
premiering
at
the
1996
<a
href="/wiki/Cannes_Film_Festival?qsrc=3044"
title="Cannes
Film
Festival">Cannes
Film
Festival</a>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson%27s_Ghosts?qsrc=3044"
title="Michael
Jackson's
Ghosts">Michael
Jackson's
Ghosts</a></i>
was
a
short
film
written
by
Jackson
and
<a
href="/wiki/Stephen_King?qsrc=3044"
title="Stephen
King">Stephen
King</a>
and
directed
by
<a
href="/wiki/Stan_Winston?qsrc=3044"
title="Stan
Winston">Stan
Winston</a>.
The
video
for
<i>Ghosts</i>
is
over
38&nbsp;minutes
long
and
holds
the
<i>Guinness
World
Record</i>
as
the
world's
longest
music
video.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350_152-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ultimate_booklet_48.E2.80.9350-152">[153]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-tara_610.E2.80.93611_161-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_610.E2.80.93611-161">[162]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-lewis28_331-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-lewis28-331">[332]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-guinness_332-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-guinness-332">[333]</a></sup></p>

<a

Jackson's
star
on
the











<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"

set
in

</div>

<p>Jackson
throughout
his
career
transformed
the
art
of
the
music
video
and
paved
the
way
for
modern
pop
music.
<i><a
href="/wiki/Daily_Telegraph?qsrc=3044"
title="Daily
Telegraph">Daily
Telegraph</a></i>
writer
<a
href="/wiki/Tom_Utley?qsrc=3044"
title="Tom
Utley">Tom
Utley</a>
described
Jackson
in
2003
as
&quot;extremely
important&quot;
and
a
&quot;genius&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-telegraph_239-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-telegraph-239">[240]</a></sup>
For
much
of
his
career,
he
had
an
&quot;unparalleled&quot;
level
of
worldwide
influence
over
the
younger
generation
through
his
musical
and
humanitarian
contributions.<sup
id="cite_ref-ADL_154-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-ADL-154">[155]</a></sup>
Jackson's
music
and
videos,
such
as
<i>Thriller</i>,
<a
href="/wiki/MTV?qsrc=3044#Breaking_the_color_barrier"
title="MTV">fostered
racial
diversity</a>
in
MTV's
roster,
helped
to
put
the
relatively
new
channel
into
public
awareness,
and
steered
the
channel's
focus
from
rock
to
pop
music
and
R&amp;B,
shaping
the
channel
into
a
form
that
proved
enduring.
Jackson's
work
continues
to
influence
numerous
<a
href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music?qsrc=3044"
title="Hip
hop
music">hip
hop</a>,
rock,
pop
and
<a
href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B?qsrc=3044"
title="Contemporary
R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a>
artists,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Patrick_Stump?qsrc=3044"
title="Patrick
Stump">Patrick
Stump</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Justin_Timberlake.2C_Usher.2C_Ne-Yo_Talk_About_Michael_Jackson.27s_Influence_333-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Justin_Timberlake.2C_Usher.2C_Ne-Yo_Talk_About_Michael_Jackson.27s_Influence-333">[334]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Jennifer_Lopez?qsrc=3044"
title="Jennifer
Lopez">Jennifer
Lopez</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-334"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-334">[335]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9_Knowles?qsrc=3044"
title="Beyonc&eacute;
Knowles">Beyonc&eacute;</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Beyonc.C3.A9.2C_Top_Stars_Tip_Their_Hats_to_Michael_Jackson_335-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Beyonc.C3.A9.2C_Top_Stars_Tip_Their_Hats_to_Michael_Jackson-335">[336]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey?qsrc=3044"
title="Mariah
Carey">Mariah
Carey</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-336"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-336">[337]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/M%C3%BDa?qsrc=3044"
title="M&yacute;a">M&yacute;a</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-337"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-337">[338]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
title="Usher
(entertainer)">Usher</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-CNN_338-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-CNN-338">[339]</a></sup>
<a

title="Adam
Lambert">Adam
Lambert</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-out_339-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-out-339">[340]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Green_Day?qsrc=3044"
title="Green

Day</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Green_Day_Look_Forward_To_Janet_Jackson.27s_VMA_Tribute_To_Michael_340-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Green_Day_Look_Forward_To_Janet_Jackson.27s_VMA_Tribute_To_Michael-340">[341]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Justin_Timberlake?qsrc=3044"
title="Justin
Timberlake">Justin
Timberlake</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-341"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-341">[342]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Britney_Spears?qsrc=3044"
title="Britney
Spears">Britney
Spears</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-rollingstone_2_342-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-rollingstone_2-342">[343]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
title="Madonna
(entertainer)">Madonna</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Is_The_Reason_343-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Is_The_Reason-343">[344]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Alien_Ant_Farm?qsrc=3044"
title="Alien
Ant
Farm">Alien
Ant
Farm</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-tara_614.E2.80.93617_165-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-tara_614.E2.80.93617-165">[166]</a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Ludacris?qsrc=3044"
title="Ludacris">Ludacris</a>,
<a

title="Ciara">Ciara</a>,<sup

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-344">[345]</a></sup>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Sean_P._Diddy_Combs?qsrc=3044"
title="Sean
P.
Diddy
Combs">Sean
P.
Diddy
Combs</a><sup
id="cite_ref-345"

href="#cite_note-345">[346]</a></sup><sup

class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-346">[347]</a></sup>
among
many
others.<sup
id="cite_ref-Ludacris_Says_Michael_Jackson_Inspired_Him_to_.27Shoot_for_the_Sky.27_347-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Ludacris_Says_Michael_Jackson_Inspired_Him_to_.27Shoot_for_the_Sky.27-347">[348]</a></sup>
BET
described
Jackson
&quot;as
quite
simply
the
greatest
entertainer
of
all
time&quot;
and
someone
who
&quot;revolutionized
the
music
video
and
brought
dances
like
the
moonwalk
to

world.
Jackson’s
sound,

and
legacy
continues
to
inspire
artists
of
all
genres.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-348"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-348">[349]</a></sup></p>








<p>Allmusic's
Steve
Huey
describes
Jackson
as
&quot;an
unstoppable
juggernaut,
possessed
of
all
the
skills
to
dominate
the
charts
seemingly
at
will:
an
instantly
identifiable
voice,
eye-popping
dance
moves,
stunning
musical
versatility
and
loads
of
sheer
star
power&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-allmusic_289-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-allmusic-289">[290]</a></sup>
In
the
mid-1980s,
<i>Time</i>
magazine's
pop
music
critic,
<a
href="/wiki/Jay_Cocks?qsrc=3044"
title="Jay
Cocks">Jay
Cocks</a>,
noted
&quot;Jackson
is
the
biggest
thing
since
<a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Beatles">The
Beatles</a>.
He
is
the
hottest
single
phenomenon
since
<a
href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley?qsrc=3044"
title="Elvis
Presley">Elvis
Presley</a>.
He
just
may
be
the
most
popular
black
singer
ever&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-TIME_39-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-TIME-39">[40]</a></sup>
In
1990,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Vanity_Fair_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
title="Vanity
Fair
(magazine)">Vanity
Fair</a></i>
cited
Jackson
as
the
most
popular
artist
in
the
history
of
show
business.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_43-44_97-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_43-44-97">[98]</a></sup>
In
2007,
Jackson
said,
&quot;Music
has
been
my
outlet,
my
gift
to
all
of
the
lovers
in
this
world.
Through
it,
my
music,
I
know
I
will
live
forever.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_in_His_Own_Words_349-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_in_His_Own_Words-349">[350]</a></sup></p>








<p>Shortly
after
Jackson's
death,
on
June
25,
2009,
MTV
briefly
returned
to
its
original
music
video
format
to
celebrate
and
pay
tribute
to
his
work.<sup
id="cite_ref-A_Star_Idolized_and_Haunted.2C_Michael_Jackson_Dies_at_50_350-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-A_Star_Idolized_and_Haunted.2C_Michael_Jackson_Dies_at_50-350">[351]</a></sup>
The
channel
aired
many
hours
of
Jackson's
music
videos,
accompanied
by
live
news
specials
featuring
reactions
from
MTV
personalities
and
other
celebrities.
The
temporary
shift
in
MTV's
programming
culminated
the
following
week
in
the
channel's
live
coverage
of
Jackson's
memorial
service.<sup
id="cite_ref-More_adds.2C_loose_ends.2C_and_lament_351-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-More_adds.2C_loose_ends.2C_and_lament-351">[352]</a></sup>
At
the
memorial
service
on
July
7,
2009,
founder
of
<a
href="/wiki/Motown_Records?qsrc=3044"
title="Motown
Records">Motown
Records</a>
Berry
Gordy
proclaimed
Jackson
as
&quot;the
greatest
entertainer
that
ever
lived&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Farewell_to_a_King_352-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Farewell_to_a_King-352">[353]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Berry_Gordy-Brings_Mourners_To_Their_Feet_With_Jackson_Tribute_353-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Berry_Gordy-Brings_Mourners_To_Their_Feet_With_Jackson_Tribute-353">[354]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_hailed_as_greatest_entertainer.2C_best_dad_354-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_hailed_as_greatest_entertainer.2C_best_dad-354">[355]</a></sup></p>








<p>In
2010,
two
university
librarians
found
that
Jackson's
influence
extended
into
<a
href="/wiki/Academia?qsrc=3044"
title="Academia">academia</a>,
and
has
been
mentioned
in
scholarly
literature
pertaining
to
a
range
of
subject
matter.<sup
id="cite_ref-Chandler_355-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Chandler-355">[356]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Hidalgo_356-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hidalgo-356">[357]</a></sup>
The
two
researchers
combed
through
various
scholars'
writings,
and
compiled
an
<a
href="/wiki/Annotated_bibliography?qsrc=3044"
title="Annotated
bibliography">annotated
bibliography</a>
of
those
writings.
The
bibliography
located
references
to
Jackson
in
research
reports
concerning
music,
popular
culture,
chemistry
and
an
array
of
other
topics.<sup
id="cite_ref-Chandler_355-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Chandler-355">[356]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Hidalgo_25_357-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Hidalgo_25-357">[358]</a></sup></p>

and

<i>Thriller</i>

<p>Michael
Jackson
was
inducted
onto
the
<a
href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame?qsrc=3044"
title="Hollywood
Walk
of
Fame">Hollywood
Walk
of
Fame</a>
in
1980
as
member
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_Jacksons?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Jacksons">The
Jacksons</a>
and
in
1984
as
solo
artist.
Throughout
his
career
he
received
numerous
honors
and
awards,
including
the
<a
href="/wiki/World_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
title="World
Music
Awards">World
Music
Awards</a>'
Best-Selling
Pop
Male
Artist
of
the
Millennium,
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="American
Music
Award">American
Music
Award</a>'s
Artist
of
the
Century
Award
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Bambi_(prize)?qsrc=3044"
title="Bambi
(prize)">Bambi</a>
Pop
Artist
of
the
Millennium
Award.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_50-53_166-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_50-53-166">[167]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_and_Halle_Berry_Pick_Up_Bambi_Awards_in_Berlin_358-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_and_Halle_Berry_Pick_Up_Bambi_Awards_in_Berlin-358">[359]</a></sup>
He
was
a
double-inductee
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_Rock_and_Roll_Hall_of_Fame_inductees?qsrc=3044#Performers"
title="List
of
Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame
inductees">Rock
and
Roll
Hall
of
Fame</a>,
once
as
a
member
of
The
Jackson&nbsp;5
in
1997
and
later
as
a
solo
artist
in
2001.
Jackson
was
also
inducted
in
several
other
hall
of
fames,
including
<a
href="/wiki/Vocal_Group_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044#Vocal_Group_Hall_of_Fame_Inductees"
title="Vocal
Group
Hall
of
Fame">Vocal
Group
Hall
of
Fame</a>
(as
<a
href="/wiki/The_Jackson_5?qsrc=3044"
title="The
Jackson
5">The
Jackson
5</a>
member)
in
1999
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Inductees_of_the_Songwriters_Hall_of_Fame?qsrc=3044#J"
title="Inductees
of
the
Songwriters
Hall
of
Fame">Songwriters
Hall
of
Fame</a>
in
2002.<sup
id="cite_ref-Nelson_George_overview_50-53_166-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Nelson_George_overview_50-53-166">[167]</a></sup>
In
2010,
Jackson
was
inducted
into
the
Dance
Hall
of
Fame
as
the
first
(and
currently
only)
dancer
from
the
world
of
pop
and
rock
'n'
roll.<sup
id="cite_ref-newstimes1_359-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-newstimes1-359">[360]</a></sup>
His
awards
include
many
<i><a
href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records?qsrc=3044"
title="Guinness
World
Records">Guinness
World
Records</a></i>
(eight
in
2006
alone),<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Named_Most_Successful_Entertainer_Of_All_Time_360-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Named_Most_Successful_Entertainer_Of_All_Time-360">[361]</a></sup>
13
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>
(as
well
as
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Legend_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="Grammy
Legend
Award">Grammy
Legend
Award</a>
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Lifetime_Achievement_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="Grammy
Lifetime
Achievement
Award">Grammy
Lifetime
Achievement
Award</a>),
26
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
title="American
Music
Awards">American
Music
Awards</a>
(including
the
&quot;Artist
of
the
Century&quot;
and
&quot;Artist
of
the
1980s&quot;)—more
than
any
artist—,
13
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_artists_who_reached_number_one_on_the_Hot_100_(U.S.)?qsrc=3044#J"
title="List
of
artists
who
reached
number
one
on
the
Hot
100
(U.S.)">number
one
singles
in
the
US</a>
in
his
solo
career—more
than
any
other
male
artist
in
the
Hot
100
era<sup
id="cite_ref-Most_No._1s_By_Artist_.28All-Time.29_361-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Most_No._1s_By_Artist_.28All-Time.29-361">[362]</a></sup>—and
estimated
sales
of
up
to
750&nbsp;million
records
worldwide,
making
him
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">world's
best
selling
male
solo
pop
artist</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-MJ_Grammy.27s_31-5"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MJ_Grammy.27s-31">[32]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-World_Records_100-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-World_Records-100">[101]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-KOP_achievements_114-6"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-KOP_achievements-114">[115]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_Poll_164-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_Poll-164">[165]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_MJ_216-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_MJ-216">[217]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_2009_217-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_2009-217">[218]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_to_add_concerts_after_sellout_362-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_to_add_concerts_after_sellout-362">[363]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Living_Legend_363-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Living_Legend-363">[364]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-Lifetime_Achievement_364-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Lifetime_Achievement-364">[365]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_Poll2_365-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_Poll2-365">[366]</a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-AMAs_Poll3_366-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AMAs_Poll3-366">[367]</a></sup>
On
December
29,
2009,
the
American
Film
Institute
recognized
Jackson's
death
as
a
&quot;moment
of
significance&quot;
saying,
&quot;Michael
Jackson's
sudden
death
in
June
at
age
50
was
notable
for
the
worldwide
outpouring
of
grief
and
the
unprecedented
global
eulogy
of
his
posthumous
concert
rehearsal
movie
<i>This
Is
It</i>.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson.27s_Death_Among_2009.27s_Major_Moments_367-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson.27s_Death_Among_2009.27s_Major_Moments-367">[368]</a></sup>
Michael
Jackson
also
received
a
Doctor
of
Humane
Letters
Degree
from
the
United
Negro
College
Fund<sup
id="cite_ref-Michael_Jackson_Achievements_368-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Michael_Jackson_Achievements-368">[369]</a></sup>
and
also
an
Honorary
Doctorate
of
Humane
Letters
from
Fisk
University.<sup
id="cite_ref-Pop_Star_Michael_Jackson_Influenced_Academics.2C_Received_PhD_369-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Pop_Star_Michael_Jackson_Influenced_Academics.2C_Received_PhD-369">[370]</a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Earnings_and_wealth">Earnings
and
wealth</span></h2>








<p>It's
estimated
that
Michael
Jackson
earned
about
$750
million
in
his
lifetime.<sup
id="cite_ref-370"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-370">[371]</a></sup>
In
the
last
several
decades
of
his
life,
sales
of
his
recordings
through
Sony's
music
unit
have
earned
him
an
estimated
$300
million
in
royalties.
He
may
have
also
earned
an
additional
$400
million
from
concerts,
music
publishing
(including
his
share
of
the
Beatles
catalog)
endorsements,
merchandising
and
music
videos.
Estimating
how
much
of
these
earnings
Jackson
was
able
to
personally
pocket
is
difficult
because
one
has
to
account
for
taxes,
recording
costs
and
production
costs.<sup
id="cite_ref-LeedsSorkin_371-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-LeedsSorkin-371">[372]</a></sup></p>








<p>There
have
also
been
several
detailed
estimates
of
Jackson's
net
worth
and
these
range
from
negative
$285
million
to
positive
$350
million.</p>

class="wikitable">

over
the

link</a></i>]</span></sup></li>










<li
id="cite_note-broadcasting-101"><a
href="#cite_ref-broadcasting_101-0">↑</a>
Press
references
to
Jackson
as
a
music
&quot;king&quot;
appeared
as
early
as
1984
after
he
swept
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Awards</a>,
and
&quot;king
of
pop&quot;
appeared
as
early
as
1987.
MTV
and
<a
href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company?qsrc=3044"
title="Fox
Broadcasting
Company">Fox</a>
used
the
title
in
joint
press
releases
and
ads
for
the
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Black_or_White?qsrc=3044"
title="Black
or
White">Black
or
White</a>&quot;
video
at
Jackson's
request,
but
MTV
denied
a
report
that
VJs
were
required
to
use
it
on-camera.
Writers
described
the
title
as
self-proclaimed
from
then
on.</li>

<script
type="text/javascript">

(function()
{




$(document).ready(function(){
	
	
		$(".preview").click(function(e){	




		window.location
=
$(this).attr('value');	








});
		




	$(".preview").hover(function(e){	




		$('#preview').empty();




		$("#preview").append("<img
id='previewImg'
src='"+$(this).find('img').attr('src')+"'
alt='Smiley
face'
"+$(this).find('img').attr('value')+"='130'/>");	




		$("#preview")
				.css("display","block")




			.css("top",$(this).position().top
+
"px")




			.css("left",$(this).position().left
+
"px")
				.css("z-index","0")




			.fadeIn("fast");
			
			$("#previewAnc")
				.css("display","block")
				.css("top",($(this).position().top
-
1)
+
"px")




			.css("left",($(this).position().left
-
1)
+
"px")
				.css("z-index","1")




			.fadeIn("fast")
				.attr('onmousedown',
$(this).attr('onmousedown'))




			.attr('href',
$(this).attr('value'));








});
		
		$("#previewAnc").mouseout(function(){
			$('#preview')
				.css("display","none")
				.css("z-index","-1")
				.fadeIn("fast")
				.empty();
			$(this).css("display","none").css("z-index","-1");
		});
	
	});
})();

</script>

function
addEvent(obj,
evType,
fn)

{
	if(obj.addEventListener)

	{

		obj.addEventListener(evType,
fn,false);

		return
true;

	}

	else
if
(obj.attachEvent)

	{

		var
r
=
obj.attachEvent("on"+evType,
fn);

		return
r;

	}
	else
	{

		return
false;

	}

}
